| 31 | 2026-05-23 | **WaySafe** | Round-7 opener: shipped the **Travel Advisory brief** ŌĆö a single-page, share-and-print safety briefing that fuses every engine in the repo (Safety Intelligence + Sentinel + Forecast + geofences + POIs) into the *one screen* a tourist actually wants before walking out the door. New `advisory.py` (~540 LOC, pure stdlib + reuse of the project's modules; reportlab only imported lazily inside `brief_to_pdf`) is the engine: (1) **`build_brief(target_lat, target_lon, target_label, *, inc_df, poi_df, geofences, forecaster, sentinel_clusters, risk_pulse, now=ŌĆ”, radius_km=2.0, lookback_days=7)`** is the single entrypoint ŌĆö pandas DataFrames or list-of-dicts both go through `_as_records()`, `compute_safety` runs identical-to-the-Map-tab physics so the score never disagrees, geofence membership is point-in-polygon-checked against every ring, recent incidents within the scan disc are coerced + ranked `(age_hours asc, severity desc)` with each row stamped with a human-readable `age` ("3h ago"), a `category_severity` lookup, status badge, and a 160-char note snippet; categories aggregated, a 7-day daily-counts trend built oldestŌåÆnewest with `bucket = min((now-ts).days, lookback_days-1)` so boundary incidents never silently drop; help POIs filtered to the `safety.HELP_POI_TYPES` set, ranked by distance, top-5 kept; Sentinel clusters with disc overlap (`d Ōēż radius_km + c.radius_km`) projected to **edge distance** `max(0, d ŌłÆ c.radius_km)` so an overlapping cluster reads as "0.0 km" not "centroid 0.6 km"; forecast windows pulled by sweeping the next 12 h hourly through `forecaster.hotspots(t, k=1)` and surfacing the **3 lowest-risk hours**. (2) **Advisory level** is computed in two stages ŌĆö base level from safety score (`0ŌĆō34 Critical ┬Ę 35ŌĆō59 Elevated ┬Ę 60ŌĆō79 Caution ┬Ę 80+ All clear`) then *force-bumped* by Sentinel: `Ōēź2 severe clusters (Critical/Emerging Ōł¦ severity_meanŌēź3.5) ŌåÆ Critical`, `Ōēź1 severe and base==All clear ŌåÆ Elevated`, because a static score can't see "things are moving in this neighbourhood" without bringing the velocity signal across. (3) **Recommendations** are built by a small priority-ordered ruleset: Critical/Elevated ŌåÆ postpone + share location; in-zone ŌåÆ name the geofence; escalating cluster nearby ŌåÆ cite its velocity status + distance + category; help POI ŌåÆ pin the nearest by type; late-night + non-All-clear ŌåÆ prefer well-lit busy streets; non-All-clear with windows ŌåÆ name the best depart label + top-cell risk %; All-clear and clean ŌåÆ standard precautions fallback so the list never goes empty. (4) Three exports are first-class: **`brief_to_json`** emits a stable `waysafe.advisory.v1` schema (target, advisory{level/color/headline/is_safe_to_go}, safety{score/band/factors/nearest_help_km/incidents_nearby}, scan{radius_km/lookback_days/trend_daily_counts}, incidents[], incidents_by_category, active_geofences, help_pois[], nearby_clusters[], best_windows[], risk_pulse{status/headline/severe_cluster_count}, recommendations[]) so two briefs can be diff'd, stored in a CRM, or piped into a downstream chatbot; **`brief_to_markdown`** is the WhatsApp/email/Notion-paste format with severity dots + verified-tick + nested note quotes; **`brief_to_pdf`** uses reportlab to render a polished single-page A4 ŌĆö colour-stripe header band lifted from the advisory hue (`_hex_to_rgb01` for clean fractional RGB), wide score-bar with band-coloured fill behind a white "Safety N / 100 ┬Ę band" label, two-column layout (left: "Why this score" factor rows + Risk-zone names ┬Ę right: "Nearest help" POIs + Safer depart windows), incident table with verified Ō£ō markers + italicised notes underneath each row, live-clusters row with edge-distance + radius + days-since-last, numbered recommendations checklist (markdown bold stripped, 95-char wrap), footer disclaimer about deferring to local authorities. **New theme component**: `theme.render_advisory_brief(brief)` ŌĆö a ~200-line render that emits the full card stack: glass **hero** card with radial-gradient glow keyed to the advisory hue + 6 px left-border + uppercase advisory stripe + conic-ring score (`--pct` driven via the same `.ws-ring` primitives `render_score_card` uses) + level headline; four **KPI tiles** (incidents nearby ┬Ę live clusters / N escalating ┬Ę safer depart window ┬Ę nearest help name+km); **two-column section row** with recent-incident pills (per-severity color dot via `_SEVERITY_HUE`, category icon, distance, age, verified/pending pill, italic note) + the 7-day trend sparkline (weekday labels aligned via `_adv_timedelta` so the labels match `now - lookback_days + 1 + i`), and on the right the cluster pill list (status pill colored by `_cluster_status_hue`, "overlapping" label when edge distance Ōēż 50 m) + safer-depart-windows rows (greenŌåÆamberŌåÆred gradient bar, hour label, percentage right-aligned); **nearest help** list with per-type emoji (`­¤Åź ­¤Üō Ō×Ģ ­¤ÜÆ Ōä╣’ĖÅ`); **numbered, accent-tinted recommendations** with lightweight `**bold**` markdown rendering. CSS lives inside `inject_theme` (additive ŌĆö 6 new selector groups under `.ws-adv-*` totalling ~140 lines: `ws-adv-hero / ws-adv-stripe / ws-adv-tiles / ws-adv-section / ws-adv-inc-row / ws-adv-spark / ws-adv-cluster / ws-adv-window / ws-adv-poi / ws-adv-rec` plus their state variants) so the new tab inherits the same dark glassmorphism every other panel uses. **App wiring**: tab labels grow from 10 to 11 (`Advisory` inserted between `Forecast` and `Sentinel` ŌĆö Sentinel/Report/Alerts/SOS/Trip-Log indices shifted down by 1 in lockstep); the Advisory tab body is a self-contained 130-line block ŌĆö three-mode `target` radio (your location / pick a POI / custom lat/lon) with a place-name field for the custom mode, a Brief-settings expander with `radius_km` (0.5ŌĆō5 km) and `lookback_days` (3ŌĆō30) sliders, a single `adv.build_brief(...)` call that re-uses the same `inc_df / poi_df / GEOFENCES / get_forecaster() / sent_clusters / sent_pulse` already computed once per rerun at the top of the Tourist View, the new `render_advisory_brief` card, and a 3-column actions row with **`Ō¼ć’ĖÅ Download PDF brief`** / **`Ō¼ć’ĖÅ Download JSON`** / **`Ō¼ć’ĖÅ Download Markdown`** download buttons that all share an auto-filename convention (`waysafe_advisory_<slug>_<YYYYMMDD_HHMM>.<ext>`), plus a "View raw markdown / JSON" expander with side-by-side code blocks for quick previews without an actual download. **Validation**: ran the engine against the live `data/incidents.csv` (38 rows) with `now=2026-04-27T10:00` and saw the expected story ŌĆö Baga Beach scores 38/100 with 14 incidents in scan, lands `Elevated` (escalating cluster pushes it up from `High Risk`), trend `[0,1,0,0,1,3,3]` sums clean to 8 (the off-by-one at the lookback edge was caught + fixed via `bucket = max(0, min(bucket, lookback_days-1))`), forecaster picks `Mon 22:00 @ 4%` as the safer window, recommendations land in the right priority order (postpone ŌåÆ geofence name ŌåÆ cite the live escalating cluster ŌåÆ pin Calangute Police @ 1.5 km ŌåÆ cite the safer depart window); | 32 | 2026-05-24 | **Credicrew** | Round-7 move: shipped the **Command Center** (`/hq`) ŌĆö the portfolio layer the whole product had been missing. Every other surface is single-role/single-candidate; a recruiter running ten reqs had no bird's-eye view. New `frontend/src/lib/portfolio.ts` (~470 LOC, pure functions, no I/O) is the aggregation engine: it takes a flattened snapshot of every role + shortlist (each candidate carrying match score, interview composite, confidence, recommendation, an optional offer draft, and an optional accept-probability) and rolls it up into one `PortfolioSummary`. Six concerns: (1) **hire-signal parity** ŌĆö re-derives `round(composite┬ĘŌłÜconfidence)` exactly as `decision.ts` so the two never disagree; (2) **aggregate funnel** ŌĆö current-status histogram across the 5-stage progression (`newŌåÆoutreachŌåÆscreeningŌåÆinterviewŌåÆoffer`, `passed` bucketed separately), reached-at-least computed by summing from the deepest stage backwards, adjacent-stage conversion = `reached(this)/reached(prev)`; (3) **comp forecast** ŌĆö `total_cash = base + signOn + base┬Ębonus%` (mirrors peer-parity's definition) summed over every drafted offer into **committed** (all sign) vs **expected** (risk-weighted by each offer's live win-probability), plus avg base / avg accept / top-spend role; (4) **per-role health** ŌĆö a renormalised weighted blend of momentum (`1 ŌłÆ stale/active`, 0.30), interview coverage (`interviewed/reached-interview`, 0.25), decision quality (`mean hireSignal/100`, 0.25), and offer confidence (`mean winProb`, 0.20) where **absent signals drop out and remaining weights renormalise** (same philosophy as the interview rubric ŌĆö a role with no offers isn't punished), plus a top-candidate pick, best composite, and a bottleneck stage (the progression stage holding the most active, Ōēź2 to qualify); (5) **cross-role talent leaderboard** ŌĆö the 8 strongest interviewed candidates across *all* roles by hire signal; (6) **attention feed** ŌĆö a priority-sorted action list: stale candidates (Ōēź14d medium / Ōēź21d high), offers tracking <45% accept (`<30%` high), signal-Ōēź75 candidates still parked in new/outreach (fast-track), roles with a shortlist but zero interviews, and empty roles ŌĆö capped at 10, highŌåÆlow. Portfolio health weights each role by its active count. **Backend mirror** in `backend/app/services/portfolio.py` (~360 LOC, pure stdlib) is byte-for-byte parity with the TS engine ŌĆö confirmed by transpiling `portfolio.ts` standalone and running an identical fixed-`NOW` 3-role / 5-candidate fixture through both: every number, ordering, funnel cell, comp total (committed 90.16 / expected 52.23 LPA), health score (rA 68 ┬Ę rB 79 ┬Ę portfolio 74), talent ranking (Dev 86 ┬Ę Asha 82 ┬Ę Esha 61 ┬Ę Chitra 28), and attention kind matched exactly (the only JSON delta is TS-omits-`undefined` vs Python-emits-`null`, the same convention every other mirror uses). New `backend/app/routers/portfolio.py` exposes `POST /portfolio/summary` accepting both `camelCase` and `snake_case` via Pydantic `Field(alias=ŌĆ”)` + `ConfigDict(populate_by_name=True)`; `main.py` version bumped `0.7.0 ŌåÆ 0.8.0` and root index advertises the route. **Frontend Command Center** at `/hq` (13.3 kB / 120 kB First Load): `gatherInput()` resolves every role's shortlist through the *existing* match/interview/offer engines (so the dashboard never disagrees with the per-role pages ŌĆö composite via `summarise()`, accept-probability via `benchmarkComp()` + `winProbability()`), then `buildPortfolio()` drives the render. Layout ŌĆö gradient title row with **Copy brief / Export brief.md** (a Markdown portfolio digest built inline: health, comp, funnel, top talent, attention); a hero row pairing a 120 px conic health ring (hue-ramped roseŌåÆamberŌåÆindigoŌåÆemerald via `HEALTH_HUE`) with a 6-tile KPI grid (open roles ┬Ę in-flight ┬Ę interviews run ┬Ę offers out ┬Ę committed comp ┬Ę stale); a full-width **funnel card** (per-stage gradient bars sized by reached/total-active with reached+here counts overlaid and a colour-graded conversion % on the right); a **role leaderboard** (sortable by health / in-flight / days-open ŌĆö each row a 48 px health ring + proportional `StageBar` segmented by `STATUS_TONE` + stale/bottleneck chips + top-candidate caption, deep-linking to the role); a **comp-forecast aside** (committed vs expected gradient bars + avg-base / avg-accept stat tiles) above a **recommendation-mix** bar reusing `TIER_HUE`; and a 2-up **talent leaderboard** (signal rings deep-linking to each scorecard) + **attention feed** (severity-toned, deep-linked cards ŌĆö offer-risk items route to Offer Studio, others to the scorecard/role; empty state reads "Nothing on fire Ō£ō"). | 33 | 2026-05-25 | **LLM_Playground** | Round-7 move: shipped **Studio Insights** ŌĆö the analytics layer the whole product had been missing. The playground could *measure* everything (Arena latency & cost, single + multi-judge composites, blind-vote ELO) and *persist* it all into `history.db`, but it never answered the one question an LLM-eval tool exists for: **which model gives the best quality per dollar?** New `backend/src/insights.py` (~430 LOC, pure stdlib + a single `from src import vote_arena` for the ELO join) is a **read-only** roll-up ŌĆö it invents no tables and writes nothing, so it's the *same numbers* History/Judge/Vote already produced, just aggregated, and can never disagree with them. `_aggregate()` walks every run once, building a per-`Provider:model` accumulator (`_Acc`, `__slots__`-only so the file's non-stdlib import surface is literally one line): appearances, success/error counts, latency/cost/token/char samples, judge composites (pulled from `payload.judge.verdicts` ŌĆö works for single-judge *and* consensus runs since `history.update_consensus` writes a back-compat `payload.judge`), and judge wins. `model_scorecards()` derives per-model `avg_cost`, `avg_composite`, `quality_per_dollar = avg_composite / avg_cost`, success rate, and an `efficiency_index` (min-max-normalised q/$ to 0-100), then joins each row to its `vote_arena.leaderboard()` ELO rating + games + win-rate. `efficiency_frontier()` computes the **Pareto frontier of maximise-quality / minimise-cost**: a model is *dominated* iff some other eligible model has `composite Ōēź mine AND avg_cost Ōēż mine` with at least one strict ŌĆö the non-dominated set is the frontier, and dominated points carry their `dominated_by` list; only models with a judge score **and** positive cost are placed (the two axes), everything else lands in `unplaced` with a `no_judge_score`/`no_cost` reason. `cost_timeline()` buckets runs to UTC-day (spend ┬Ę runs ┬Ę judged ┬Ę avg-top-score), `provider_rollup()` aggregates to provider level (spend share + mean quality), and `build_insights()` stitches it all into one payload with a headline `summary` (total spend, best-value/top-quality/cheapest/fastest/top-ELO picks, and a 7-day spend trend anchored on the *latest run's* timestamp so it's deterministic). **One new endpoint** `GET /api/insights?min_appearances=N` returns the whole bundle in a single read. **Frontend**: new `components/InsightsPanel.jsx` (~640 LOC) is a 7th sidebar mode (**Insights**, indigoŌåÆemerald `new` badge, `Gauge` icon). A **Copy brief** button emits a Markdown digest of the whole dashboard. `App.jsx` gains the radio option + a panel branch (the Library "new" badge moves to Insights); `services/api.js` gains `insights({minAppearances})`. **Validation**: deterministic engine smoke test against a seeded temp DB (3 runs, 4 models, 1 vote) asserts every number ŌĆö avg composites (gpt-4o 89.0 from [90,88], haiku 82.0), q/$ (flash 71000, haiku 41000), the dominated `o-mini` (0.012/65) correctly excluded from the frontier with `dominated_by=["OpenAI:gpt-4o"]` while gpt-4o/haiku/flash all sit on it, frontier sorted cost-ascending, ELO joined (gpt-4o games=1, judge_wins=2), timeline = 3 days with avg-top-score 90.0 on day 0, provider spend-share summing to 100.0%, summary best-value=flash / top-quality=gpt-4o / cheapest=flash, and an empty-DB guard returning `scorecards=[]` + `frontier=[]`. | 34 | 2026-05-26 | **SynapseOS** | Round-7 move: shipped **Synthesis** ŌĆö auto-written, cited topic briefings per cluster. Day 9 made clusters *visible* (greedy-modularity communities) and *named* (distinctive-term TF-IDF), but a violet blob labelled "embeddings" still isn't knowledge ŌĆö you had to open every member note to learn what the topic actually *said*. Synthesis closes that gap. New `backend/app/synthesis.py` (~430 LOC, pure stdlib + the existing `embed`/`community`/`store`/`llm` modules ŌĆö no new deps) builds a brief straight from a cluster's members: (1) **centroid** = mean of member embeddings, L2-normalized so plain dot-product is cosine; (2) **cohesion** = mean `cosine(member, centroid)` Ōłł [0,1] ŌĆö a real "how tight is this topic" signal that doubles as a split-me-up hint when low; (3) **harvest** splits every member body into sentences and scores each by `cosine(sentence, centroid) + 0.04┬Ękey_term_hits + 0.02┬Ęsource_centrality`; (4) **select** runs MMR-style dedup (drop any candidate whose cosine to an already-picked sentence > 0.86) with a two-pass diversifier that prefers one sentence per distinct note before backfilling ŌĆö top 3 ŌåÆ **overview**, next 5 ŌåÆ **key claims**; (5) **compose** orders the overview sentences by their source note's centrality and stitches them into prose, every sentence carrying an inline `[#N]` citation into a Sources list numbered by centrality (so `[#N]` is stable + clickable); (6) **open threads** = member notes phrased as questions (title or a body sentence ends in `?`) plus *under-developed* members (body < 140 chars, or zero intra-cluster synapses computed from edges with both endpoints inside the cluster); (7) **bridges** = notes in *other* clusters with `cosine(note, centroid) Ōēź 0.16` that the synapse graph hasn't linked to any member ŌĆö cross-pollination the graph is one Žä-nudge from drawing, each carrying its own cluster id/name/colour. Degenerate cases handled: a stub-only cluster falls back its most-central note's opening line; a singleton cluster reports cohesion 1.0 and skips bridges/threads. **Optional LLM mode** (`SYNAPSE_LLM_KEY`) rewrites the overview under a strict contract (use ONLY numbered sources, every sentence ends `[#N]`, 2ŌĆō3 sentences Ōēż80 words) ŌĆö and we *reject* any LLM answer that drops its citations, falling back to extractive so synthesis never loses its receipts. `to_markdown()` renders a self-contained portable brief; `serialize()` ships the dataclasses as JSON. **Two new endpoints** in `main.py`: `GET /digest?cluster_id=&threshold&top_k&mode` (404s cleanly when the id doesn't exist at the given params) and `GET /digest/export.md?cluster_id=ŌĆ”` (Content-Disposition attachment, slugified filename). `schemas.py` gains `ClusterDigestOut` + 4 nested models. **Frontend**: new `components/Synthesis.tsx` (~430 LOC) ŌĆö a centered modal tinted with the cluster's own colour, a **cohesion ring** (conic-gradient, same idiom as the brief's score ring), the synthesis paragraph with `[#N]` markers parsed into **clickable superscript citation chips** (`ref` renamed off the reserved React prop name so the click handler actually fires), key-claim bullets, an **open-threads** list (`?` amber for questions, `ŌŚŗ` pink for stubs, each opening the source note), a **bridges** list (target-cluster chip + cosine %), a numbered **sources** list, an **extractive/Ō£© llm** mode pill, and a **Ōżō md** export anchor. `TopicPalette.tsx` grew a per-row ŌØŹ **synthesize** button (appears on hover, tinted the cluster colour) wired through a new `onSynthesize` prop; | 35 | 2026-05-27 | **Titan** | Round-7 close: shipped **Model Validation** (`/validation`) ŌĆö the regulator-grade model-risk layer (SR 11-7 / FFIEC) that answers the one question every prior surface dodged: *is the detection engine actually any good?* New `apps/ai-aml/backtest.py` (~430 LOC, pure stdlib, zero ML deps) replays `risk.score_accounts` against a **labelled** set of confirmed outcomes and reads the trade-off. Labels accept either a positive-id list (every other scored party = benign ŌĆö the confirmed-SAR setup) or a `{id: 0\|1}` dict that restricts the population to adjudicated accounts only. It computes the **full confusion matrix at every cut 0ŌĆō100** (TP/FP/FN/TN ŌåÆ precision ┬Ę recall ┬Ę specificity ┬Ę F1 ┬Ę F╬▓ ┬Ę balanced-accuracy ┬Ę Youden's J), rank-based **ROC AUC** via an exact Mann-Whitney U over all pos├Śneg pairs (no sampling, no seed), step-wise **average precision**, an **F╬▓-optimal recommended cut** (╬▓=2 default ŌĆö a missed launderer outweighs an extra review), and the move that pays for itself: **per-detector discrimination**, each of the eight rules' *own* single-feature AUC over the positive-vs-negative intensity distributions ŌĆö surfacing which rules carry the signal (sanctions 0.83, velocity 0.81) and which are near-random noise (round-amount Ōēł0.55) so re-weighting is evidence-led. A `verdict` block grades the model (strong/fair/marginal/poor) and writes plain-English notes ("lowering the cut to 7 lifts recall 75%ŌåÆ100%"; "N known-bad accounts slip under the current cut"). Crucially it honours a candidate `weights` override, so a what-if hypothesis from the day-1 simulator is *validated*, not just admired ŌĆö boosting the under-weighted fan detectors recovers the mule at higher precision than blindly dropping the threshold, and the headline tiles show the ╬ö-vs-canonical to prove it. Endpoints `POST /aml/backtest` + `GET /aml/backtest/sample` (43-tx labelled set: 8 confirmed-bad across five typologies + two hard cases ŌĆö an under-detected smurf = recall miss, a benign payroll account that trips the weak round-amount rule = false-positive trap). | 36 | 2026-05-28 | **WaySafe** | Round-8 opener: shipped **Compass ŌĆö Destination Showdown**, the *comparative* counterpart to the Advisory tab. The Advisory answers "is **this** place safe?"; Compass answers the question tourists actually agonise over ŌĆö "**where** should I go tonight: Baga or Anjuna? stay in Calangute or move to Panaji?" New `compass.py` (~460 LOC, pure-stdlib + reuse of `safety` / `forecast` / `sentinel`, zero new deps) is the engine. **`compare_destinations(targets, *, inc_df, poi_df, geofences, forecaster, sentinel_clusters, now, depart, radius_km)`** runs every engine over 2ŌĆō5 candidates **at the chosen depart time** and folds three signals into one forward-looking **Compass score** (`compass = clip(safety_score ŌłÆ 16┬Ęforecast_risk_at_depart ŌłÆ cluster_penalty, 0, 100)`): the static `compute_safety` score is the base; the **forecast term** prices *when* you'd arrive via `forecaster.risk_at(lat, lon, depart)` (a calm beach at 3 PM ŌēĀ the same beach at 2 AM); the **cluster term** folds in Sentinel *velocity* ŌĆö for every cluster whose disc overlaps the destination's scan radius, `status_weight(Critical 12 ┬Ę Emerging 6 ┬Ę Steady 2 ┬Ę Cooling 0) ┬Ę severity_mean/5`, summed and capped at 20 ŌĆö so an escalating hotspot drags a destination below its historical score (the advisory's "things are moving" rule, made quantitative). Per-card **advisory level** mirrors `advisory._LEVEL_TABLE` exactly (incl. the Ōēź2-severe-clusters force-bump to Critical) so Compass and Advisory never disagree. `assess_destination` also harvests geofence membership, nearest help POI (name + km), and the **safer hour to visit *that* spot** via `forecaster.risk_curve` argmin. Candidates rank by compass desc ŌåÆ fewer incidents ŌåÆ closer help; the `_verdict` helper scales the headline by margin (`clear safe pick` Ōēź15 ┬Ę `edges it` Ōēź5 ┬Ę `just shades it` Ōēź1 ┬Ę `neck-and-neck` <1) and names the **deciding factor** as the largest per-factor goodness gap in the winner's favour ("wins mainly on nearest help"). Each destination carries five `FactorScore`s (safety ┬Ę forecast ┬Ę incidents ┬Ę help ┬Ę clusters) with a 0ŌĆō1 *goodness* for heat-mapping. | 37 | 2026-05-29 | **Credicrew** | Round-8 opener: shipped the **Calibration Studio** (`/roles/[id]/calibration`) ŌĆö the panel-fairness layer every interview surface had been missing. Until now every scorecard assumed a *single* rater (one composite, one verdict); real hiring runs panels, and the loudest hidden source of unfair decisions is uncalibrated interviewers ŌĆö lenient vs. severe, flat/central-tendency, or simply off-consensus ŌĆö so a candidate's fate turns on *who* happened to interview them. New `frontend/src/lib/calibration.ts` (~560 LOC, pure functions) models interviewers ├Ś candidates ├Ś rubric-dimensions and computes: (1) **per-rater bias** ŌĆö *leniency* = mean deviation from the per-cell panel consensus (signed +lenient/ŌłÆsevere), *spread* = population stdev of their ratings (near-zero ŌćÆ central-tendency "flat"), and *consensus correlation* = Pearson r against the cell means (low ŌćÆ off-consensus), each auto-flagged `lenient`/`severe`/`flat`/`contrarian`; (2) **panel reliability** ŌĆö a variance-based **consensus index** (`mean(1 ŌłÆ cellVar/4)` over multi-rated cells) for cell-level agreement *plus* **ICC(1)**, an *unbalanced one-way* intraclass correlation over the candidate├Śdim cells (handles panels where different candidates were seen by different interviewers, which a balanced targets├Śraters matrix can't) measuring how much rating variance is real candidate signal vs. rater noise; (3) the same ICC recomputed on **de-biased** ratings (each rater's leniency subtracted) ŌĆö the headline insight: on a biased panel the lift is dramatic (the seed lands **ICC 0.00 ŌåÆ 0.34**), proving calibration restores the panel's power to discriminate; (4) **raw vs. calibrated composites + rank shifts** ŌĆö each candidate gets a raw consensus composite and a de-biased one (rater offsets removed before averaging), revealing that when the lenient EM only saw juniors and the severe staffer only saw seniors, the raw ranking *compresses* the real gap and calibration reorders the boundary candidates; (5) **disagreement hot-cells**, per-candidate flags (`single_rater`/`high_disagreement`/`thin`), an overall verdict (`calibrated`/`minor_drift`/`needs_calibration`/`unreliable`), suggestions and a Markdown report. New `frontend/src/lib/panel_seed.ts` builds a deterministic, deliberately **unbalanced** 4-person seed panel (Meera Nair┬Ęlenient EM ┬Ę Arjun Verma┬Ęsevere staff ┬Ę Sana Khan┬Ęcalibrated senior ┬Ę Dev Menon┬Ęflat lead) hashed from role+candidate+dim so it's idempotent and lights the studio up on first open; Sana+Dev anchor the consensus while Meera sees only the lower-scoring half and Arjun only the upper half, manufacturing exactly the bias calibration then corrects. **Backend mirror** in `backend/app/services/calibration.py` (~430 LOC, stdlib only ŌĆö `math`+dataclasses) is **byte-for-byte parity** with the TS engine, *verified* by transpiling `calibration.ts` standalone via the TypeScript compiler API and diffing a fixed 6-candidate / 90-rating fixture through both engines (every rater stat, cell, composite, rank, consensus index, raw+calibrated ICC and verdict matched exactly ex-timestamp); new `backend/app/routers/calibration.py` exposes `POST /calibration/summary` accepting `camelCase` (TS-engine `as_dict`) and `snake_case` (curl) via Pydantic `Field(alias=ŌĆ”)` + `ConfigDict(populate_by_name=True)`. API version bumped `0.8.0 ŌåÆ 0.9.0`; root index advertises the new route. **Frontend Calibration Studio** at `/roles/[id]/calibration` (14.2 kB / 121 kB First Load): gradient fuchsiaŌåÆsky title row with Manage-panel / Copy-report / Export-report.md; a 5-tile headline (verdict ┬Ę consensus index ┬Ę ICC with `ŌåÆ de-biased` delta ┬Ę rank shifts ┬Ę biased-rater count); new `CalibrationBias` component (diverging severeŌåÉŌåÆlenient bars per interviewer with spread/consensus-r chips + flag pills); new `RankShiftChart` (an SVG **bump chart** connecting each candidate's raw rank ŌåÆ calibrated rank, climbs in emerald / drops in rose, with composite + ╬ö labels); new `AgreementGrid` (candidate ├Ś dimension heatmap tinted by agreement via a roseŌåÆamberŌåÆemerald `agreementHue`, hot-cells ringed, **click any cell to inspect every rater's rating and edit it inline 1ŌĆō5** ŌĆö bias, ranking and reliability all recompute live off a `useMemo`); new `PanelDrawer` (add/remove interviewers ŌĆö new ones auto-scored on the whole shortlist via a chosen archetype ŌĆö + reset-to-seed); a hot-cell list and an actions/notes panel. Theme: ~10 new `.cc-cal-*` selectors in `globals.css` (verdict/ bias/ bump radial-gradient accents, cell hover scale, inspector glow, drawer slide reusing the existing `cc-parity-slide` keyframe). | 38 | 2026-05-30 | **LLM_Playground** | Round-8 move: shipped **Eval Suites** ŌĆö the regression-test layer every prior surface in the playground had been missing. Arena measures *one* prompt ├Ś N models, Judge scores it, Consensus debiases it, Vote ELOs it, History persists it, Library versions it, Insights aggregates it ŌĆö but nothing in the studio let you run the **same fixed battery of cases** against every candidate model and watch for *regressions* when you change a prompt or swap a model. That's what real LLM-ops needs and what every commercial tool (Braintrust, Langfuse, PromptLayer) builds first; the playground now has it natively. New `backend/src/evals.py` (~720 LOC, pure-stdlib + `ThreadPoolExecutor`) models *suites* (named, ordered case lists with tag/star/desc), *cases* (a user prompt + AND-combined pass criteria: `expected_contains`, `expected_not_contains`, `expected_regex` via `re.search`, `expect_json` that strips ```json fences before `json.loads`, `judge_min` composite threshold), *runs* (one execution against a provider+model with optional judge), and *case_results* (response, status, latency, cost, judge composite + rationale, pass bool, and a per-criterion `reasons[]` array ŌĆö every rule's `{kind, expected, ok, detail?}` so the UI never has to guess *why* a case failed). The engine fan-outs cases through a 6-worker pool ŌĆö a 12-case suite finishes in ~2├Ś the slowest call, not 12├Ś ŌĆö then runs a parallel judging pass that reuses the existing `judge_compare` path so the math is provably identical to the Arena's `/judge` endpoint. **Schema** lives in the same `history.db` (single backup captures everything): `eval_suites` + `eval_cases` (with re-packed `idx` on delete so the UI stays gap-free) + `eval_runs` + `eval_case_results`, all guarded with `CREATE IF NOT EXISTS` and bulletproof child-row cleanup on `delete_suite` regardless of `PRAGMA foreign_keys` state. Aggregates: `pass_rate`, `avg_composite`, `total_cost`, `wall_latency` (max-parallel) vs `total_latency` (serial-sum) so the UI can show **the parallelism dividend**. **`compare_runs(a, b)`** joins cases by `case_id` first, falling back to `case_idx` (so a renamed case still pairs), and produces per-case `delta.composite` + a `delta.passed` of **+1 = fixed**, **ŌłÆ1 = regressed**, **0 = same** ŌĆö a single column tells you whether the new model fixed cases or broke them. **`seed_smoke_suite()`** is idempotent and seeds a 6-case starter battery (factual recall ┬Ę refusal ┬Ę JSON formatting ┬Ę arithmetic ┬Ę summarisation `judge_min: 70` ┬Ę code synthesis regex) so a brand-new user presses *Run* in 10 seconds and sees every column populate. **16 new routes** in `routes/llm.py` (`POST/GET/DELETE /api/suites`, `/seed`, `/stats`, `/<id>/meta`, `/<id>/cases` + `/<id>/cases/<cid>` (POST=update, DELETE=delete), `/<id>/cases/reorder`, `/<id>/runs` (POST=execute, GET=list), `/runs/<rid>` (GET=detail, DELETE), `/runs/compare`) all wired into `api.js` with a matching narrow client. **Frontend Eval Suites panel** (`components/EvalSuites.jsx`, ~1100 LOC): a gradient indigoŌåÆvioletŌåÆfuchsia hero header; a 5-tile **stats banner** (suites ┬Ę cases ┬Ę runs+avg-pass ┬Ę spend ┬Ę best-model crown by avg pass-rate across all its runs); a left-rail **suite list** with per-row stats (case count ┬Ę run count ┬Ę last-run-relative ┬Ę model:provider chip + pass-rate bar pinned to the latest run) and a starred-only toggle; a right-pane that swaps between an empty state (with a "**Seed Smoke Test**" CTA + blank-suite alternative ŌĆö first-click delight) and a full **suite workspace** stacking *Suite header / Run Config panel / Case list editor / Recent runs / Run report / Compare drawer*. The **Run Config panel** (`Provider` + `Model` selects auto-populated via `/api/models/<provider>`, an optional system prompt that's applied to every case, and a `judge` switch that reveals judge provider+model selects with the same wiring) issues one `/runs` call and toasts the pass-rate verdict on return. The **Case editor** is a single grid with `Must contain` / `Must NOT contain` / `Regex match` / `Response must parse as JSON` switch / `Judge min (0-100)` / note, validates the prompt is non-empty, and saves to either `/cases` (new) or `/cases/<cid>` (edit). The **Case row** renders a chip-row of every criterion with a 1-char glyph (`+ ŌłÆ / {} Ōēź Ō£ō`) so the suite's *intent* is readable in two seconds; **smoke-only** cases (no criteria) get a single `Ō£ō non-empty response` chip ŌĆö the engine and the UI agree on what "no criteria means pass". The **Run report** is four gradient KPI tiles (Pass-rate ring + breakdown ┬Ę Avg-composite + judged-share ┬Ę Total cost + per-case ┬Ę Wall-time + serial-sum), a **criteria breakdown** card that pivots every AND-combined rule across all cases ("`regex` passed 4/5 ┬Ę `judge_min` passed 3/5") with mini pass-rate bars per kind, and an accordion of per-case rows whose collapsed state shows pass chip + composite + cost + latency + the per-criterion reason chips and whose expanded state lays out *prompt | response | judge rationale* side-by-side. The **Compare drawer** picks two runs of the same suite (UI: a `vs` button per run row that cycles AŌåÆB), fetches `/runs/compare`, and renders a 3-column summary (A ┬Ę B ┬Ę BŌłÆA delta ŌĆö pass-rate / composite / cost / wall-time, with **invert=true** on cost+latency so cheaper/faster reads green), then a per-case table with PassChip-per-side ┬Ę ╬ö-composite ┬Ę and a **"fixed | regressed | same"** column with up/down/minus icons. App wiring: a new **"Suites"** radio at the bottom of the sidebar (FlaskConical icon, `new` gradient ribbon) + a render branch at the top of the main-column switch (`selectedMode === 'suites' ŌåÆ <EvalSuites />`). **Validation**: `pnpm build` clean (1729 modules ŌåÆ 606 kB gzip:171 kB); a Flask `test_client` walked all 10 user-paths end-to-end against a monkey-patched `FakeProvider` (seed ŌåÆ list ŌåÆ detail ŌåÆ create ŌåÆ add case ŌåÆ run ŌåÆ stats ŌåÆ update case ŌåÆ second run ŌåÆ compare ŌåÆ delete) ŌĆö every status code 200/201, the seed run reported `pass=5/6 rate=83.33%` with the 5th case correctly failing on `judge_min: 70` without judging enabled and the per-criterion reason `"judge_min:N ┬Ę no judge run for this case"` proving the engine surfaces *why* every case fails. | 39 | 2026-05-31 | **SynapseOS** | Round-8 move: shipped **Tensions ŌĆö where your second brain disagrees with itself** ŌĆö the contradiction-surfacing layer no PKM tool has. Every prior surface reveals what *agrees* (synapses link, clusters bind, Synthesis paraphrases the consensus); none surface where the graph *contradicts itself*, and that's the highest-value PKM signal ŌĆö a note that says "boring tech wins" sitting next to "that framework was a mistake" is an *unreconciled belief*, exactly the thing a thinking partner should flag. New `backend/app/tensions.py` (~600 LOC, pure stdlib, zero new deps) is the engine. For every pair `(a, b)` with `cosine(a, b) Ōēź floor` (default `0.18`, tuned slightly above Žä so tensions are pulled from the *connected* graph not random buzzword collisions), it runs four detectors and emits a `Tension` when any fire with non-trivial weight: (1) **polarity** ŌĆö hand-tuned valence lexicons (POSITIVE `good ┬Ę best ┬Ę ship ┬Ę wins ┬Ę works ┬Ę scale ┬Ę ŌĆ”`, NEGATIVE `bad ┬Ę worst ┬Ę breaks ┬Ę fails ┬Ę overrated ┬Ę slow ┬Ę ŌĆ”`) plus a one-content-word negation window that flips local valence ("not bad" ŌåÆ positive, "not great" ŌåÆ negative) so the naive bag-of-words doesn't get reversed by hedging; fires when `sign(pol_a) ŌēĀ sign(pol_b)` *and* `min(|pol_a|, |pol_b|) Ōēź 1` so a single polar word per side doesn't trip the rule, weight = `min(1, span/6)`; (2) **antonym** ŌĆö a 28-pair lexicon (simple/complex, fast/slow, overrated/underrated, robust/brittle, durable/fragile, ŌĆ”) checked against each side's word set, weight saturates at two pairs because contradictions aren't additive; (3) **contrast** ŌĆö both-sided contrast cues (but, however, although, instead, rather, actually, ŌĆ”); a "but" on *one* side is just writing, a "but" on *both* means each is qualifying the other's frame, weight = `min(1, 0.3 + 0.15┬Ę(min(ca,cb)ŌłÆ1))`; (4) **title-clash** ŌĆö explicit "Against X" vs "Why X works" with light singular/plural stemming (`folder Ōēł folders`, the most common plural that originally broke obvious pairs) and stopword filter (so "the" doesn't crown a false match), *plus* opposite-polarity titles with a shared non-polar topic token. The **title-clash bypass** lets unambiguous title contention surface even *below* the cosine floor ŌĆö the hashing-trick embedder is what it is, and a deterministic linguistic signal shouldn't be overridden by `cosine = 0.04`. `magnitude = clip(cosine ┬Ę (1 + ╬Ż weights), 0, 1)` so cosine sets the ceiling and signals scale within it. Each emitted `Tension` carries: `kind Ōłł {internal, cross}` (same-cluster ŌĆö where you expected agreement and got conflict ŌĆö vs philosophical disagreement across topics), the firing `signals[]` with per-signal `(kind, weight, detail)`, two `evidence` quotes (one per side, the **most-polarized sentence in each note in the direction of that note's own stance** ŌĆö picked via per-note pre-pass over sentence-split bodies, fallback to opening sentence for neutral framings), and a `bridge_title + bridge_prompt + bridge_tags` triple auto-generated from the firing signal kinds ("When X applies vs when Y" for antonym pairs, "Reconciling: X Ōåö Y" for polarity, "Bridge: X & Y" otherwise) so **Reconcile** is one click. **Two new endpoints**: `GET /tensions?floor=&limit=&threshold=&top_k=` returns the full report (threshold ┬Ę floor ┬Ę total_pairs_scanned ┬Ę candidate_count ┬Ę tension_count ┬Ę tensions[] ┬Ę stats with internal/cross counts and top_magnitude), `GET /tensions/export.md` ships the same report as a portable artifact (sectioned by Inside-a-cluster / Across-clusters, both quotes with `Ōåæ/Ōåō` arrows, signal line, **Reconcile:** prompt) ŌĆö paste into Notion / journal / anywhere. New Pydantic schemas (`TensionSignalOut`, `TensionEvidenceOut`, `TensionOut`, `TensionReportOut`); API version bumped `0.2.0 ŌåÆ 0.3.0`. **Frontend Tensions modal** (`components/Tensions.tsx`, ~530 LOC): roseŌåÆviolet header strip (rose because contradiction, not violet because not just-another-cluster), a custom logo glyph (two circles connected by a jagged disagreement line), **3 filter chips** with live counts (all / inside a cluster / across clusters) and an `Ōżō md` export link; per-tension **card** with a magnitude meter bar at the top (roseŌåÆpink gradient with `box-shadow: 0 0 12px {accent}55` to read as "alive"), a 3-column headline grid (`title A | Ō¤Ę | title B`) where each title is clickable to inspect the note and shows its cluster color-dot + name, a `kind` micro-label and `magnitude% ┬Ę cos N%` readout in the middle column, **signal chips** with a one-char glyph (`ŌåĢ Ōćä ŌēĀ ŌĆ╝`) + label (`stance / antonyms / but-cues / title clash`) + the engine's `detail` string, a **2-column evidence grid** (one quote per side, italic with `border-left: 2px solid {accent}66`, `Ōåæ/Ōåō/┬Ę` polarity arrow in lime/rose/grey), and a **suggested bridge** panel with the title/prompt and a gradient cyanŌåÆviolet **Ōż┤ Reconcile** button that fires `onReconcile(draft)`. The composer is extended to accept an optional `draft` prop: on receive it pre-fills `(title, body, tags)`, **scrolls itself into view with `requestAnimationFrame` + `scrollIntoView`** so the user lands on the form, **focuses the body textarea** with `setSelectionRange(0,0)` so typing immediately appends to the prompt, and shows a 2.2s pulse ŌĆö a rose ring + shadow + `Ōż┤ reconciling` floating chip ŌĆö to confirm what just happened. **Header trigger** is a rose-bordered pill (`Ō¤Ę tensions`) with a live count badge (the page does a cheap `api.tensions({ limit: 50 })` probe after every graph refresh and renders `N` or `99+`) ŌĆö *your second brain has N unresolved contradictions* is now a glanceable header stat. **Seed extended** with two notes that manufacture a tension on first run ("Unit tests are underrated" vs the existing "The test pyramid is overrated", and "Why folders work" vs the existing "Against the folder") so the modal isn't empty on cold start; the seed graph now contains 18 notes and surfaces **5 tensions** (3 internal ┬Ę 2 cross ┬Ę top magnitude 0.44) at default settings ŌĆö covering all four signal types (antonym, polarity, contrast, title-clash). **Validation**: `npx tsc --noEmit` clean across the new component + every existing one; `next build` clean (Route `/` 32.6 kB ┬Ę First Load JS 120 kB ┬Ę 4 static pages); FastAPI `TestClient` smoke green (`/health 200`, `/graph 200`, `/communities 200`, `/orphans 200`, `/search 200`, `/brief 200`, `/tensions 200`, `/chat 200` ŌĆö every pre-existing endpoint still works); a full schema-shape test asserts all 14 required keys per tension, polarity arrows present in markdown, floor sweep is monotonic (`{0.05 ŌåÆ 15, 0.10 ŌåÆ 12, 0.18 ŌåÆ 5, 0.25 ŌåÆ 2, 0.4 ŌåÆ 1}`), empty-DB and single-note edge cases return `tension_count = 0` cleanly. They cannot catch the inverse failure mode: **accounts whose recent behavior no longer matches their own historical baseline** ŌĆö sleeper takeovers, mule recruitments, slow operator shifts where the line itself moved, no single transaction crossed it. New `apps/ai-aml/drift.py` (~720 LOC, pure stdlib, zero new deps) is the engine. For each account it splits transactions into a **baseline** + **current** window (configurable: `baseline_fraction` 0.2ŌĆō0.9 or an explicit ISO `split_at`; the latter lets an analyst test their own "I think it started here" hypothesis against the data) and computes a fingerprint across **ten distribution-distance axes**: (1) **`amount`** ŌĆö two-sample Kolmogorov-Smirnov on tx amounts, weight `0.18`; (2) **`hour`** ŌĆö Jensen-Shannon divergence on a 24-bucket hour-of-day histogram (normalised by ln 2), weight `0.14`; (3) **`dow`** ŌĆö same JS on a 7-bucket day-of-week histogram, weight `0.10`; (4) **`direction`** ŌĆö abs delta in inflow/total ratio scaled so a 50pp swing saturates, weight `0.10`; (5) **`velocity`** ŌĆö abs log-ratio of tx-per-active-day scaled by log 5 (a 5├Ś spike saturates), weight `0.08`; (6) **`cparty_diversity`** ŌĆö abs delta in Herfindahl-Hirschman of counterparty share, weight `0.08`; (7) **`cparty_novelty`** ŌĆö share of current counterparties **never seen** in the baseline window (the single most-predictive axis in real laundering ŌĆö clean accounts don't suddenly grow new payee lists), weight `0.12`; (8) **`geo`** ŌĆö total-variation distance between baseline-mix and current-mix geo vectors, weight `0.08`; (9) **`round_rate`** ŌĆö abs delta in % of round-amount transfers (` >= 1k and amt % 1k == 0`), weight `0.05`; (10) **`median_shift`** ŌĆö abs logŌéé shift of median amount scaled by 3 (an 8├Ś change saturates), weight `0.07`. Weights sum to exactly 1.0 (`assert` on import). Composite `overall = clip(╬Ż wßĄó ┬Ę scoreßĄó, 0, 1)` mapped to five verdict bands: `stable <0.18 ┬Ę mild <0.35 ┬Ę drifting <0.55 ┬Ę erratic <0.75 ┬Ę transformed Ōēź0.75`. The engine also derives: **drivers** (axes whose contribution clears `DRIVER_FLOOR ┬Ę overall`, top 3), an auto-generated **narrative** that strings together the top-driver `detail` + new-counterparty list + median-shift line + inflow/outflow flip + change-point onset, a **suggested_action** keyed off verdict ("escalate ŌĆö promote to a case at high priority and confirm account-holder identity" at the top end), a **counterparty contribution table** (top 8 sorted with brand-new entrants first, each row with `baseline_count/current_count/baseline_volume/current_volume/is_new/activity_lift/volume_lift`), and a **change-point estimate**: walks the current window day by day, computes KS of the trailing 7-day slice against the *full baseline*, reports the earliest day above `CHANGE_POINT_KS_FLOOR = 0.30` (with `n >= 3` in the slice) as `onset_iso + days_ago`. The full rolling-KS series ships with the response so the frontend draws a curve with a dashed-floor guide and a pulsing onset dot. **Three new endpoints** in `apps/ai-aml/main.py`: `GET /aml/drift/rules` (auditor view of weights, bands, dim labels, every tunable), `GET /aml/drift/sample` (a deterministic three-account demo ŌĆö `ACC-STABLE` routine vendor pattern, `ACC-MILD` gentle growth, `ACC-DRIFT` 18-week sleeper that wakes up into a 9-day round-amount burst ŌĆö plus a `recommended_split_at` ISO timestamp so the demo teaches the tool), `POST /aml/drift` (`{ transactions, account_id?, baseline_fraction?, split_at? }` ŌåÆ portfolio-ranked report or single-account detail; portfolio mode skips accounts with `< MIN_BASELINE_TXS(6) + MIN_CURRENT_TXS(3)` on either side and surfaces them in `skipped[]`). Engine version bumped `titan-aml/1.6.0 ŌåÆ 1.7.0`. **Gateway**: three pass-through routes in `apps/api/main.py` (10 s timeout for the cheap `rules`/`sample` GETs, 30 s for the `/aml/drift` POST since portfolio mode over a large book can run the engine 20├Ś in one call). **API client**: ~150 LOC of new TS types in `apps/frontend/lib/api.ts` covering `DriftVerdict ┬Ę DriftDimensionKey ┬Ę DriftDimension ┬Ę DriftCounterparty ┬Ę DriftChangePoint ┬Ę DriftWindow ┬Ę DriftReport ┬Ę DriftPortfolioSummary ┬Ę DriftResponse ┬Ę DriftRules ┬Ę DriftSample` plus `getDriftRules() ┬Ę getDriftSample() ┬Ę runDrift()`. **Frontend `/drift` console** (`app/drift/page.tsx`, ~620 LOC; **page bundle 8.91 kB ┬Ę First Load JS 96 kB**): a glass-strong **hero strip** (round-8 ┬Ę day-40 ribbon, gradient headline, Load-demo + Run-analysis buttons, auto-loaded demo with the recommended split pre-set so the page is *never* empty on first visit); a controls section with a CSV textarea (live row count) + scope toggle (Portfolio ┬Ę Single-account) + a window-split control that flips between a fraction slider (`0.2ŌĆō0.9`, step `0.05`) and an explicit ISO timestamp; a **6-tile portfolio summary** (accounts ┬Ę drifters ┬Ę per-verdict counts) tinted with the verdict hex; a **ranked left-rail** (per-row verdict pill + gradient bar + composite %, click to swap the active report); and the showpiece ŌĆö the **active report**: a verdict-tinted **hero ring** (132px conic-gradient on `var(--drift-accent)`, glowing via `ws-drift-ring-glow` for `drifting/erratic/transformed`, the headline + plain-English narrative + recommended-action block beside it), the **`DriftRadar`** (`components/DriftRadar.tsx`, 10-axis polar SVG ŌĆö baseline silhouette pinned to the outer rim as a dashed teal reference, current silhouette plotted **inwards** by `1 - score` so a perfectly-matching axis lands on the rim and a fully-drifted axis collapses to the center; labels tint rose at `score >= 0.4` so the visual reads at a glance with no legend), the baseline + current **window cards** (median ┬Ę inflow share ┬Ę unique cparts ┬Ę active days ┬Ę ISO date range), a **per-dimension breakdown** (sorted by contribution desc; each row a 3-col grid with label + engine-supplied detail, a tri-stop gradient bar ŌĆö tealŌåÆsky < 0.25, amberŌåÆorange < 0.5, orangeŌåÆrose otherwise ŌĆö and `score ┬Ę weight ┬Ę contrib` mini-stats), the **hour-of-day** + **day-of-week** baseline-vs-current overlays (`components/DistributionOverlay.tsx` ŌĆö paired bar charts, hollow teal outline for baseline, filled rose for current, peak-normalised so the comparison reads regardless of volume; the 24-bar version label-thins to every 3rd hour), the **change-point timeline** (`components/DriftTimeline.tsx` ŌĆö rolling-KS curve with a shaded area, dashed amber floor line, the onset day rendered as a larger amber dot, before/after labels), and the **counterparty contribution table** (sticky header, brand-new rows tagged with a rose `new` chip + show `+Ōł×` in the volume-╬ö column instead of `nan`). **Theme**: 55 new lines of `.ws-drift-*` CSS under the existing dark-glass system ŌĆö five `ws-drift-verdict-{verdict}` classes that set two CSS custom properties (`--drift-accent`, `--drift-accent-tint`) so the hero strip's radial gradient + the ring's box-shadow glow all retheme by swapping one className; five `ws-drift-pill-{verdict}` chip palettes; `.ws-drift-dim-row:hover` (`translateX(1px)` + background lift); a `ws-drift-pulse` keyframe used by the change-point onset dot. **Layout** picks up a new `Drift` nav entry between `Network` and `Validation`. **Home page** gains a 7th feature card (`Behavioral Drift ŌĆö anomaly ┬Ę catches what threshold rules miss`) and the stats strip swaps `Workflow states` for `Drift axes: 10`. **Validation**: `npx tsc --noEmit` exit 0 across the new page + 3 components + the API-client additions; `next build` clean (12 routes, `/drift` 8.91 kB ┬Ę 96 kB First Load, every pre-existing route unchanged, shared chunks steady at 87.1 kB); FastAPI `TestClient` smoke green (`/healthz` reports `titan-aml/1.7.0`, `/aml/drift/rules` weights sum to exactly 1.0, `/aml/drift/sample` returns 243 txs + the highlight account + recommended split, `/aml/drift` portfolio mode lands `ACC-DRIFT` at overall 0.5347 ŌåÆ `drifting`, `/aml/drift` with the recommended split lands it at 0.8416 ŌåÆ `transformed`, `/aml/drift` rejects empty payload with 400, and every pre-existing endpoint ŌĆö `/aml/rules`, `/aml/score`, `/aml/backtest/sample`, `/aml/typologies` ŌĆö still answers 200); engine-level edge-case sweep (empty input, insufficient-tx skip, single-account scope, Z-suffix `split_at`, byte-identical determinism via `json.dumps(sort_keys=True)`, every dimension schema has all 8 required keys, weights-sum invariant asserted at import time). README extended: a new top-of-file **"Day-40 ŌĆö Behavioral Drift"** quote block, three new endpoint rows in the API table, a full **"Behavioral drift, in detail"** section (inputs ┬Ę ten-axes table ┬Ę composite formula ┬Ę verdict-band table ┬Ę change-point logic ┬Ę counterparty view ┬Ę bundled demo ┬Ę determinism), a new `/drift` row in the frontend route table, `drift.py` added to the `ai-aml/` module tree, three new frontend components added to the layout tree, a `~~behavioral-drift / anomaly layer~~` roadmap item ticked. | 41 | 2026-06-02 | **WaySafe** | Round-9 opener: shipped **StaySafe ŌĆö Accommodation Safety Picker**, the *bookable* counterpart to Compass. Compass answers "where should I *go* tonight?" ŌĆö a single-point-in-time visit. StaySafe answers "where should I *sleep*?" ŌĆö a fundamentally different question because you spend 16+ hours/day at a stay across the sleep / evening-return / morning-depart windows. New `stays.py` (~580 LOC, pure-stdlib + reuse of `safety` + `forecast`, zero new deps) is the engine. **Six 0..1 sub-dimensions** scored per candidate, composite = weighted sum ├Ś 100: (1) **`sleep`** ŌĆö mean blended risk 22:00ŌåÆ06:00 on check-in date (weight 0.30); (2) **`evening`** ŌĆö mean 19:00ŌåÆ22:00 (0.20); (3) **`morning`** ŌĆö mean 06:00ŌåÆ09:00 (0.10). Each window is a **45/55 blend** of `forecaster.risk_at(when)` (DOW├Śhour patterns) and `safety.point_risk(when)` (static incident proximity + geofence + late-night + help-POI physics) so a stay surrounded by recent verified incidents is *always* downgraded even when the forecaster has no late-night history for that cell. (4) **`walkability`** (0.18) ŌĆö mean goodness over (hospital / police / clinic) walk legs with ceilings 4 / 2 / 1.5 km; **gracefully degrades to 2-of-3** when the dataset has no clinic POIs (the project's POI set has only hospitals + police, so this matters in practice). (5) **`quiet`** (0.12) ŌĆö inverse Sentinel cluster pressure within 0.8 km of the property, with night-active clusters (peak_hour Ōłł [20..3]) carrying a **1.6├Ś multiplier** so loud-by-night hotspots can't hide behind quiet-by-day. (6) **`reach`** (0.10) ŌĆö **U-shaped** distance to the trip's own centre of gravity (mean of the candidate stays' coords; falls back to attraction POIs, then any POI); sweet spot 1.5 km, full penalty under 0.2 km (too central / crowded) or beyond 6 km (too isolated). **Geofence floor**: if the property sits inside a risk-zone polygon the composite is forced to Ōēż 59 (Elevated) regardless of the per-window math. **Four traveller profiles** rebalance the dimension weights ŌĆö Solo (sleep 0.32, evening 0.24, morning 0.08, walk 0.18, quiet 0.10, reach 0.08), Couple (default), Family-with-kids (walk 0.22 + quiet 0.16), Business/solo-F (sleep 0.34) ŌĆö and `compare_stays(profile=...)` plugs them in. Verdict layer: ranks 2..8 candidates (compass score desc ┬Ę then better worst-window ┬Ę then closer hospital), names the winner with margin ("Recommend Vivanta Goa Panaji ŌĆö 14 pts clear of Lemon Tree Amarante Candolim"), surfaces the **deciding factor** via the largest *weight-multiplied* goodness gap in the winner's favour, and produces a one-line plain-English **why_pick** per stay assembled from the actual numbers (e.g. "Hospital 1.2 km away; calm sleep window."). **JSON** (`waysafe.staysafe.v1`) and **markdown** exports for WhatsApp / email / Notion paste. **Frontend**: new `StaySafe` tab between Compass and Sentinel (existing tab indices 7..11 shifted to 8..12). The render stack ŌĆö `theme.render_staysafe` (~180 LOC theme additions, ~250 LOC of `.ws-stay-*` CSS) ŌĆö opens with a **hero card** (winner's 0ŌĆō100 ring, level chip, profile chip, check-in/nights/N-stays meta, `+pts ahead` margin), a **podium row** of stay cards (rank chip ┬Ę kind chip ┬Ę level chip ┬Ę score bar ┬Ę sleep/evening/morning tri-cell ┬Ę **24-hour risk sparkline** with one bar per hour hue-coded greenŌåöred by risk ┬Ę headline blurb ┬Ę `why_pick` rationale below a dashed divider), a **three-column walk-to-help** card for the winner only (hospital / police / clinic each as name + distance + walk-time at 4.8 km/h + goodness bar), and a **heat-mapped factor matrix** (stays as columns, factors as rows, every cell hue-coded greenŌåöred by goodness with a sub-cell showing the **weighted points contribution** so users see *which* dimension is driving the score). Below the matrix: a per-stay text breakdown in an expander + JSON/markdown download buttons. **Demo data**: new `data/stays.csv` ships 15 curated Goa stays (premium resorts ITC Grand Goa / Hyatt / Taj Holiday Village / Park Hyatt / Radisson Blu / Vivanta / Lemon Tree / Mayfair ┬Ę mid-tier The Park Calangute / Whispering Palms / Anjuna Beach Resort ┬Ę hostels Mantra Anjuna + The Hosteller Vagator + Old Quarter Hostel ┬Ę homestay Casa Britona). On the bundled incidents.csv with the corridor seed + Family-with-kids profile + Tue 15:00 check-in, the engine ranks Vivanta Goa Panaji (urban, GMC 1.2 km / police 0.4 km) at **88/100 All-clear** vs Lemon Tree Amarante Candolim at 79 vs The Park Calangute at 59 Elevated (forced floor ŌĆö inside the demo corridor geofence) ŌĆö a clear, defensible verdict that exercises every dimension. **Validation**: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(...)"` clean on all three modified files (`app.py`, `theme.py`, `stays.py`); end-to-end engine test (load 15 stays ŌåÆ compare 6 across two profiles ŌåÆ JSON round-trip + markdown render) produces meaningful differentiation (88 vs 79 vs 76 across profiles, reach goodness varying 0.0..0.84 once the centroid is the candidate-mean); `render_staysafe` exercised with a captured-stdout mock streamlit and produces 27 K of HTML across 6 markdown blocks with every expected CSS marker present (`ws-stay-hero ┬Ę ws-stay-podium ┬Ę ws-stay-matrix ┬Ę ws-stay-card ┬Ę ws-stay-spark ┬Ę ws-stay-legs`); `streamlit run app.py --headless` boots clean (HTTP 200 on `/_stcore/health`, no init-time exceptions). README rewritten with a new top-of-features StaySafe bullet, a dedicated **"StaySafe ŌĆö Accommodation Safety Picker (Day 41)"** section (six-dimension table with formulas + defaults, profile re-weighting table, verdict surface walkthrough, exports). |

| 42 | 2026-06-03 | **Credicrew** | Round-9 move: shipped **Channel Studio ŌĆö Sourcing Intelligence**, the missing top-of-funnel surface. Every other Credicrew surface analyses what happens *after* a candidate is already in pipeline (match ┬Ę interview ┬Ę calibration ┬Ę decision ┬Ę offer ┬Ę peer parity ┬Ę portfolio health) ŌĆö none of them answer the question that sits *above* all of it: *where should I spend my next hour of outreach?* New `frontend/src/lib/sources.ts` (~430 LOC, pure functions, no new deps) is the engine. **Eight-channel taxonomy** ŌĆö `linkedin_outreach ┬Ę referral ┬Ę job_post ┬Ę agency ┬Ę community ┬Ę university ┬Ę ai_sourcing ┬Ę silver_medal` ŌĆö with per-channel labels, blurbs, and **default cost-per-touch** (`agency` 60k dominates, `linkedin_outreach` 4k, `job_post` 1k, `silver_medal` 1k ŌĆ”) reflecting how recruiters actually spend. **Four-dial ROI** ŌĆö every channel scored on (a) **quality** `0.4┬ĘmeanMatch + 0.4┬ĘmeanComposite + 20┬ĘmeanWinProb` with absent-component re-normalisation (so a channel without offers yet isn't unfairly punished ŌĆö same philosophy as the interview rubric), (b) **conversion** `100┬Ę(1 ŌłÆ e^(ŌłÆ12┬ĘreachedOffer/count))` so 25% to-offer Ōēł 90 / 10% Ōēł 60 / 5% Ōēł 35, (c) **cost efficiency** `100 ŌłÆ 0.085┬ĘcostPerOffer(Ōé╣k)` so Ōé╣50k/offer Ōēł 95 / Ōé╣500k Ōēł 40, (d) **speed** `clip(120 ŌłÆ 2.5┬ĘmeanDaysToOffer, 0, 100)`. Composite **ROI** = `0.4┬Ęquality + 0.3┬Ęconversion + 0.2┬Ęcost + 0.1┬Ęspeed`, banded `scale Ōēź 70 ┬Ę steady Ōēź 50 ┬Ę experiment Ōēź 35 ┬Ę cut < 35` with `count < 4` short-circuiting to `experiment` (the engine never recommends "scale" from a single data point). **Per-channel funnel** ŌĆö five-stage cumulative reached counts + adjacent-stage conversion rates. **Diversification** = normalised Shannon entropy across channel counts (`< 0.5` triggers concentration-risk alert). **Per-channel recommendation** strings written from the actual numbers ("Cost-per-offer Ōé╣230k is too high ŌĆö pause Recruiter agency unless quality lifts.", "Highest-quality + highest-converting channel ŌĆö double InMail seats / referral bonuses here this quarter."). **Top-level recommendations** surface: strongest `scale` channel, weakest `cut` channel, **concentration-risk** flag when one channel owns > 55% of the active pipeline, promote-to-experiment flag for thin-but-high-quality channels (count Ōēź 2, quality Ōēź 70). **Markdown brief** for standup / budget review. | 43 | 2026-06-04 | **LLM_Playground** | Round-9 move: shipped **Rubrics Studio** ŌĆö the missing first-class layer underneath every existing judge surface. The playground has had eight surfaces that *score* things (Arena, single judge, multi-judge consensus, blind Vote, History, Library, Insights, Eval Suites) but only one rubric type: an inline `[{name, description, weight}]` list that returns one composite per candidate. Domain evaluation needs more ŌĆö RAG needs "Groundedness" with a 0-anchor that calls out unsupported claims; code review needs "Edge cases" with anchors that distinguish nil-handling from concurrency-safety; support needs "Tone" with explicit blame-the-customer 0-anchors. New `backend/src/rubrics.py` (~870 LOC, pure-stdlib + reuse of `history`'s DB path/lock + `pricing.estimate_cost`) models *rubrics* (named, tag/star/desc + a `current_revision_num` pointer), *revisions* (append-only chain of `(dimensions_json, judge_addendum, note, parent_revision)` ŌĆö like `prompt_versions`), and *judgements* (the log of every "Test this rubric" call: prompt, response, per-dim scores with rationales, summary, judge latency + cost + tokens). **Dimension model**: each dimension carries `{name, weight, description, anchors: {0,5,10}}` ŌĆö anchors are 0/5/10 textual descriptors the judge prompt serialises *verbatim* so the LLM scores against an explicit yardstick, not its own intuition. `_normalise_dimensions` clamps weights to Ōēź0, re-packs them to **integer percents summing to exactly 100** using the largest-remainder method (deterministic, UI sees clean integers, composite math doesn't drift), and clips field lengths so the schema stays sane. **Judging engine**: `build_rubric_judge_prompt` renders dimension blocks (`weight%`, description, anchor rows with level-coloured backgrounds in the UI's preview) + the user prompt + optional system prompt + optional judge addendum + the response under inspection + a strict JSON output schema. `_JUDGE_SYSTEM` is a single calibrated paragraph forcing 0-10 range usage ("a mediocre response should land near 5, a refusal or off-topic answer should land near 0-2"). `parse_rubric_response` strips ```json fences, walks balanced `{...}` blocks, tolerates case-insensitive dim keys, clamps every score to [0, 10], and falls back to zeros + a sentinel rationale + `parsed_ok: false` when the judge's JSON is malformed ŌĆö the UI surfaces the failure with a `judge JSON malformed ŌĆö scored as 0s` chip instead of silently scoring 0. `_composite` is the *server-side* truth ŌĆö `╬Ż (score_i / 10 ├Ś weight_i / 100) ├Ś 100` clipped to 0..100, computed from per-dim scores and the *rubric's* weights, so a misbehaving judge can never poison the headline number. **Revisions**: `update_rubric` computes a deterministic signature over `(dimensions, judge_addendum)` and short-circuits identical-payload saves with no change-note as no-ops (no revision bump, no DB write) ŌĆö meta-only edits go through `set_rubric_meta` (no revision). `restore_revision` copies an older revision's dimensions forward as a new revision so r1 ŌåÆ r4 = "we restored r1, and now r4 is the current" ŌĆö history stays honest. **Schema** lives in the same `history.db` (single backup captures everything): `rubrics` + `rubric_revisions` + `rubric_judgements`, all guarded with `CREATE IF NOT EXISTS` and indexed on `updated_at DESC`, `starred`, `(rubric_id, revision_num DESC)`, `(rubric_id, created_at DESC)`, `(candidate_provider, candidate_model)`. **Concurrency**: shares `history._DB_LOCK` (non-reentrant `threading.Lock`); the no-op path in `update_rubric` deliberately exits the `with` block before calling back into `get_rubric` to avoid the deadlock that catches every "lock + helper-call" refactor (caught by my own first test run ŌĆö bug fixed before commit). **Aggregates** mean something: `list_rubrics` attaches per-row `n_dimensions`, `dimension_names`, `n_judgements`, `avg_composite`; `get_rubric` adds `total_cost`, `recent_judgements[8]`, the full revision chain. `stats()` exposes `n_rubrics`, `n_starred`, `n_judgements`, total spend, average composite, the **best candidate model** across all judgements (min 3, ordered by avg composite desc), the **top rubric** by usage, and the **top 5 judges** with usage / avg composite / avg latency / total spend. **Seed**: `seed_rubrics()` is idempotent ŌĆö Code Review (40/20/20/20), RAG Faithfulness (40/25/20/15), Customer Support (30/30/25/15), Creative Writing (30/25/25/20), each with full anchors written for the actual failure modes ("Doesn't compile / runs but produces wrong output / hallucinated APIs" at the 0 mark on Correctness; "Multiple confident claims absent from the context" at the 0 mark on Groundedness). Existing rubrics by the same name are left alone on re-seed; Code Review is starred so the first-launch UI immediately surfaces something. **13 new routes** in `routes/llm.py`: `GET/POST /api/rubrics`, `POST /api/rubrics/seed`, `GET /api/rubrics/stats`, `GET/DELETE /api/rubrics/:id`, `POST /api/rubrics/:id/meta`, `POST /api/rubrics/:id/revisions` (save-iff-changed), `POST /api/rubrics/:id/revisions/:n/restore`, `POST /api/rubrics/:id/test` (the judging engine), `GET /api/rubrics/:id/judgements`, `DELETE /api/rubrics/judgements/:jid`. **Frontend `RubricsStudio.jsx`** (~1180 LOC; sits between Suites and the bottom of the sidebar): a glass-strong **hero banner** (indigoŌåÆvioletŌåÆfuchsia gradient with radial-glow corners, Round-9 ribbon, "Build the yardstick the judge uses" headline, new-rubric + seed CTAs) wraps a 5-tile KPI strip (Rubrics ┬Ę Judgements ┬Ę Avg composite ┬Ę Total spend ┬Ę Best model crown) that morphs the moment any rubric is judged. Two-column body: **left rail** ŌĆö search-input + tag-Select + starred Switch + a scrollable rubric list where each card shows the score ring of the rubric's avg composite, dim count, judgement count, last-updated, tag chip with deterministic-hue background; a starred-only filter; below the list a **Top Judges** widget (provider-coloured dot ┬Ę uses ┬Ę avg latency ┬Ę spend ┬Ę avg composite). **Right pane** ŌĆö a three-tab card (**Builder ┬Ę Test ┬Ę History**, tab-bar styled as gradient-pill on active) with the rubric's name, description, tag, current revision badge, judgement count, and average composite chip in the header. **Builder tab**: a weight-distribution widget (sum chip green at 100 with a check, amber otherwise with the "normalised to 100% on save" hint; a stacked horizontal bar visualising each dimension's slice with hue-rotated bands), then the dimension rows ŌĆö each row a card with up/down arrow rail, name input, weight `Slider` (0..100 step 1) wired to a 12-char mono readout, description input, expand button that reveals the 0/5/10 anchor textareas (each level chipped with the right tinted gradient ŌĆö rose for 0, amber for 5, emerald for 10 ŌĆö so the UI teaches the user how to think about anchors), trash button. Below the dim list, an "Add dimension" button and the judge-addendum textarea (sparkle icon). A persistent **save bar** at the bottom: change-note input + Revert + Delete + Save buttons; the Save button's label flips between "Create rubric / Save revision / Save meta" based on what actually changed and is disabled when nothing did. Below that, a collapsible **Revision history** drawer (current rev chipped emerald ┬Ę older revs grey ┬Ę per-row note + relative time + dim count + parent-revision link + single-click Restore). **Test tab**: judge provider + judge model selects (model list lazy-loaded per provider via the existing `/api/models/:provider`), optional candidate provider + model fields, optional system prompt, user prompt + response textareas (response is mono-font, 140px min-height for paste). Hitting Run renders a **Verdict card** ŌĆö a 72px composite ScoreRing on the right, the "/100" headline, the judge's one-line summary in italics; below, one row per dimension with the dim name + weight % chip + score in colour-coded mono (emerald Ōēź7, amber Ōēź4, rose <4) + a hue-rotated progress fill bar + rationale + `contributes N.N pts to composite` micro-stat; a footer strip with latency, cost, total tokens, and which judge model produced it. **History tab**: judgement log per rubric with the same ScoreRing, candidate-model label, judge model, revision number, latency + cost chips, summary in italics, per-dim chips colour-coded by score (each chip's tooltip is the dim's rationale), and a `<details>` block per row to expand the original prompt + response. **API service** picks up 8 new methods (`listRubrics`, `createRubric`, `seedRubrics`, `rubricsStats`, `getRubric`, `setRubricMeta`, `saveRubricRevision`, `restoreRubricRevision`, `testRubric`, `listRubricJudgements`, `deleteRubric`, `deleteRubricJudgement`). **Sidebar nav** picks up a `Rubrics` entry between `Suites` and bottom, with a Scale icon and a gradient `NEW` ribbon. **Validation**: `vite build` clean (1730 modules transformed, no warnings beyond the pre-existing chunk-size hint); FastAPI smoke pass ŌĆö `/api/health` 200, `POST /api/rubrics/seed` returns 4 rubrics, `GET /api/rubrics` lists 4 with proper tag + dim-count + n_judgements, `GET /api/rubrics/stats` reports `n_rubrics=4, n_starred=1, n_judgements=0`, `GET /api/rubrics/:id` returns full rubric with revisions and recent judgements, `POST .../revisions` with identical payload + no change-note correctly does *not* bump the revision number (no-op detected, rev stays at 1), a real weight-shift bumps to r2 with the change note in the revision row, `restore_revision(rid, 1)` creates r3 carrying the r1 dimensions, `DELETE` cascades cleanly through child rows. | 44 | 2026-06-05 | **SynapseOS** | Round-9 move: shipped **Echo ŌĆö semantic deduplication studio**. Every prior surface in SynapseOS treats similarity as a virtue (synapses draw it, communities cluster it, Synthesis paraphrases it, Chat retrieves along it); Echo flips the sign. As a second brain matures you accumulate near-duplicates ŌĆö the same insight rewritten weeks apart ŌĆö and those polyphonic restatements pollute the graph (false hubs), inflate cluster sizes, and dirty search. New `backend/app/echo.py` (~540 LOC, pure-stdlib + reuse of the existing embedder / `store._conn` / `_pack`) is a pure function of `(notes, embeddings, threshold, skips)`: pair cosines Ōēź `Žä` (default **0.72**, configurable per-call) form an undirected edge set; **single-linkage union-find** yields connected components of size Ōēź 2 (single-linkage is intentional ŌĆö if AŌēłB and BŌēłC, you want A and C in the same merge UI even when A and C only just miss the bar themselves); `MAX_CLUSTER_SIZE=6` caps runaway hubs by keeping the most-interconnected N members; a `MIN_PEAK_COSINE=0.55` floor drops "technically similar" clusters at low thresholds. Per cluster Echo reports: **redundancy %** (mean pairwise cosine), **peak cosine**, **wasted_chars** = `chars_total ŌłÆ chars_unique` (back-of-envelope chars recovered by merging ŌĆö used as the cluster sort key so the biggest win is on top), and **canonical_id** = the member with the highest centrality (sum of cosine to the rest of the cluster), tie-broken by longest body then oldest id ŌĆö i.e. "the note that already says most of what the others say". The **merged payload** walks canonical ŌåÆ others, **fuzzy-buckets** every sentence across all members by content-word **Jaccard Ōēź 0.55** (stop-words stripped, leading bullets / numbering stripped, trailing punctuation stripped), greedily attaches each new sentence to the first bucket that clears the bar and unions its signature, then emits one representative per bucket in canonical-first encounter order. The representative prefers a canonical occurrence, else the longest phrasing ŌĆö so the merged body reads like the canonical augmented with what the duplicates contributed, not a Frankenstein paragraph. Tag union is canonical-first, capped at 8; title prefers a longer rewrite that contains the canonical title as a substring (a later restatement is usually more polished). A `dedupe_skips` SQLite table (lazy-created via `_ensure_skips_table`, primary-keyed on the normalized `(low, high)` pair so the same pair can't be inserted twice in opposite order) persists "no, those two are different" decisions forever ŌĆö subsequent `/echo` calls filter them out. **Seven new HTTP routes** in `main.py`: `GET /echo?threshold=&limit=` returns the full report, `POST /echo/preview` rebuilds the merge payload against a user-chosen `(note_ids, canonical_id)` without persisting (powers the live preview when the user flips canonical or drops a member), `POST /echo/merge` does the real work ŌĆö embeds the new body, `UPDATE`s the canonical row **in place** (id preserved so external bookmarks resolve), `DELETE`s the duplicates, recomputes the graph once to report `final_synapses` ŌĆö returning `{ merged_note_id, merged_title, deleted_ids, wasted_chars_recovered, final_synapses }`. `POST /echo/skip` accepts `{ pairs: [[a,b], ŌĆ”], reason? }` and bulk-inserts via `INSERT OR IGNORE`; `GET /echo/skips` lists; `DELETE /echo/skip?a=&b=` forgets one; `GET /echo/export.md` renders the full brief as a portable Markdown artifact (one section per cluster with all bodies + the suggested merged body). All endpoints surface clean 404/422 on missing-id / single-member requests. New schemas: `EchoMemberOut`, `EchoPairOut`, `EchoSentenceOut`, `EchoClusterOut`, `EchoReportOut`, `EchoPreviewRequest`, `EchoMergeRequest`, `EchoMergeResult`, `EchoSkipRequest`, `EchoSkipResult`, `EchoSkipEntry`. **Frontend `components/Echo.tsx`** (~580 LOC, teal/amber palette against the existing rose/violet of Tensions so the two modals are visually distinguishable in the header): a glass modal with a **cluster rail** on the left ŌĆö each row shows the redundancy bar (cyanŌåÆamber gradient), `ŌłÆN chars` recoverable badge, peak cosine ŌĆö and a **detail pane** on the right featuring an active-cluster header (the canonical title + a 3-stat strip: recoverable chars ┬Ę sentence overlap % ┬Ę cohesion %), a **member grid** where each card paints **duplicate sentences in cyan with a ring-1 `<mark>` element** (case-insensitive substring search per fuzzy bucket, longest-first so overlapping spans don't fight) and exposes "Ōśģ canonical" / "ŌłÆ exclude" controls so the user can override the auto-pick or drop a member out of the merge, a **pairwise cosine ladder** rendered as labelled rule-bars, and an **editable merge preview** card with the merged title + body textareas + merged-tag chips. **Live recompute**: every flip of canonical / drop of a member fires a debounced `POST /echo/preview` so the recoverable-char count and merged-tag union reflect what `Merge` would actually persist. The action bar pairs **Mark distinct** (calls `/echo/skip` on every pair in the cluster, dismisses) with **Merge N into #X** (the gradient CTA, shows merging spinner, flashes `merged ŌåÆ #X ┬Ę N dupes removed ┬Ę M chars recovered` toast, refreshes the graph). A Žä slider + 4 preset chips (`loose 0.60` ┬Ę `default 0.72` ┬Ę `tight 0.80` ┬Ę `exact 0.88`) let the user sweep the brief live without a refresh. A `Ōżō md` button hits the markdown export. Empty state is a tasteful "your notes are well-differentiated at this threshold ŌĆö lower Žä or add more notes". **Header** picks up a `Ōī¼ echoes` button between `tensions` and `daily brief` in the same gradient-pill family, with a badge that shows the live cluster count via a `/echo?limit=20` probe wired into the graph-refresh effect (same pattern as the tensions badge). **Page wiring**: new `echoOpen` / `echoCount` state in `page.tsx`, mounts the `<Echo>` modal next to `<Tensions>`, plumbs `onMutated ŌåÆ refreshGraph` so a merge or skip instantly rewires the canvas. **Seed**: three deliberate near-duplicate notes added to `seed.py` (Cosine substrate restated against the "Embeddings as memory" original, SQLite-is-enough restated against "SQLite is underrated", Atomic-notes restated against "Zettelkasten in one sentence") so the demo lights Echo up on first run with 2 clusters / 195 chars recoverable / 33% peak sentence overlap at default Žä. **Validation**: TypeScript `tsc --noEmit` clean across the whole frontend tree; `next build` clean (4 static pages, page bundle 37.7 kB, total first-load 125 kB ŌĆö within 0.1 kB of the previous build); FastAPI integration via `TestClient` confirms all seven routes end-to-end: `GET /echo` returns 1+ clusters at the seeded thresholds, `POST /echo/preview` honors a `canonical_id` override, `POST /echo/skip` then `GET /echo` correctly filters the pair, `DELETE /echo/skip` re-exposes it, `POST /echo/merge` collapses two notes into one (note count went from 21 ŌåÆ 19 in the smoke test, deleted_ids matched the non-canonical member, wasted_chars_recovered matched the preview), `GET /echo/export.md` returns valid Markdown with the right content-type. Live dev server (`uvicorn` + `next dev`) booted clean against each other; page server-renders with no console errors and the `/echo` probe fires on first paint. **README** picks up a new dedicated "Echoes" feature section (mirroring the Tensions section's depth ŌĆö single-linkage motivation, canonical pick formula, sentence-bucketing semantics, in-place merge semantics, the `dedupe_skips` persistence model), the full 7-route API table addition, an updated architecture diagram (`echo.py` added under `tensions.py`), and a one-line mention in the "What's in the box" list. |
