| 69 | 2026-06-30 | **SynapseOS** | Round-14 move: shipped **Compass ŌĆö Question-Anchored Lens & Research Sessions**, the surface every prior SynapseOS lens left to either Chat (one-shot RAG that forgets) or Trails (a path you've already walked). Compass closes the gap with a *persistent research session*. **The product split**: every prior surface in SynapseOS is either *observational* (Atlas / Pulse / Chronicle / Tensions / Echoes / Synthesis describe what's already in your graph) or *generative-writing* (Spark / Distill / Atomize propose or commit new notes); Compass is *generative-reading* ŌĆö pin one question, the entire vault re-ranks against it, a citation-stitched working answer assembles beneath you as you mark notes read **for this question** (a per-question read marker, not the global `last_seen_at`). **Backend** (`backend/app/compass.py`, ~440 LOC, pure-stdlib, reuses the existing `embed.embed` + `embed.cosine` so the lens lives in the same vector space as the synapse graph). **Per-note relevance** = `0.65┬Ęcosine + 0.25┬Ęlexical_jaccard + 0.10┬Ętitle_hit`, floored at `0.06` (tuned to the hash-trick embedder's conservative cosine range ŌĆö real "semantically related" pairs land between 0.10 and 0.25 in this space). **Best excerpt** per note = the body sentence with highest content-word overlap to the question, asymmetric scoring (`inter / |q_words|`) so a long sentence with one matching word still beats a short noise sentence. **Info gain** = `relevance ┬Ę (read ? 0.30 : 1.00)` ŌĆö re-skims still surface, just at lower priority, so the queue actually moves forward. **Coverage is mass-weighted, not count-weighted**: `relevance_mass_read / relevance_mass_total` ŌĆö marking the top-1 most-relevant note read can jump coverage from 0 ŌåÆ 35% if it dominates the relevance distribution. That's the right framing ŌĆö "you've answered the question," not "you've read 1/N notes." **Working answer** is the headline output: extractive on purpose ŌĆö every line is verbatim from one of your notes, every claim carries an inline `[n]` citation that resolves back to a clickable note jump, the same `(question, reads)` always produces the same answer. Capped at `WORKING_ANSWER_MAX_CITATIONS=6` and `WORKING_ANSWER_MAX_CHARS=1400` so the panel stays scan-able. **Sub-themes**: mine top distinctive content-words across the top-12 most-relevant notes (drop stopwords, <5-char terms, pure digits, and the question's own content-words to avoid trivial domination), rank by note-frequency tie-broken by peak relevance, dedup at 5-char stem prefix, take 3 survivors. Each carries `covered / note_count` for per-term coverage ŌĆö *which* sub-aspect is answered vs. cold. **Frontiers** = top 3 un-read in-lens notes by info_gain, the "read next" panel separate from the full queue so the next decision is one click. **Storage**: two new tables ŌĆö `compass_questions(id, text, created_at, archived_at)` and `compass_reads(question_id, note_id, read_at)` PK `(question_id, note_id)` with an `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE SET read_at` upsert so re-marking refreshes the timestamp; `reads_for(qid)` joins against `notes` so deleted notes get lazy-cleaned out of dangling rows. **API** (7 routes): `GET /compass/questions` lists every active question with its **current** coverage % (single batch lens compute reusing one graph/community pass across all questions), `POST /compass/questions {text}` creates and returns the **full lens** in one call (collapses the would-be two-roundtrip create ŌåÆ fetch dance), `GET /compass/questions/{id}` recomputes the lens, `POST /compass/questions/{id}/read {note_id}` marks read for this question *and* mirrors into the global `last_seen_at` so the Daily Brief doesn't keep nagging you about a note you just engaged with via Compass, `DELETE /compass/questions/{id}/read/{note_id}` unmarks (gracefully no-ops if already absent so the FE doesn't split error handling), `DELETE /compass/questions/{id}` hard-deletes + cascades reads, `GET /compass/questions/{id}/export.md` ships the paste-anywhere working-answer brief (question ┬Ę coverage % ┬Ę working answer ┬Ę sources ┬Ę sub-themes ┬Ę frontiers ┬Ę full queue). **Frontend** `frontend/src/components/Compass.tsx` (~660 LOC). Left rail: cyan/violet **QuestionComposer** with `ŌīśŌåĄ` to pin + textarea, then **QuestionList** with active questions ŌĆö each card carries a horizontal **coverage bar** (cyanŌåÆviolet gradient that brightens when active), reads-count, and a hover-revealed delete `Ō£Ģ`. Right panel: **LensHeader** with the pinned question rendered at headline size + a 5-pill stats strip (`in lens ┬Ę read ┬Ę frontiers ┬Ę top relevance ┬Ę pinned date`) bridged by a 24├Ś24 **CoverageRing** (SVG dashoffset animation, cyanŌåÆviolet gradient stroke, large coverage % in the centre). **SubquestionsRow** renders 3 sub-theme cards each with a horizontal coverage bar and a one-word state badge (`untouched / in progress / answered`); click jumps to that sub-theme's most-relevant note. **WorkingAnswerCard** is the centrepiece ŌĆö wrapped in a cyan-glow shadow, renders the answer prose with inline `[n]` citation pills (`renderAnswerWithCitations` walks the answer with a `/\[(\d+)\]/g` regex, replacing each match with a button keyed to its citation), and below shows a 2-column grid of citation rows (`[n]` marker + title + relevance + excerpt). **FrontiersCard** lists the top 3 unread notes ranked 1-2-3 in amber numerals, each with title (clickable to canvas), title-hit badge, cluster dot+name, the best excerpt, a relevance bar, the cos/lex/relevance numbers, and a prominent `Ō£ō mark read` button. **QueueCard** lists the full ranked queue with `all / unread / read` filter pills (each carrying its own count chip); every **QueueRow** carries a 7├Ś7 SVG **RelevanceDial** (lime if read, cyan if unread, 0ŌĆō100 inside), title + cluster dot + title/read badges, snippet, the cos/lex/relevance/info-gain numbers, tags, and a context-aware `Ō£ō mark read` / `Ōå║ unread` button at the right. **Compass glyph**: SVG compass rose with rotating needle in a cyan/violet/amber gradient tile. **Loading state**: dedicated **CompassSpinner** + "triangulating the lens ŌĆ”" copy. **Empty state**: ­¤¦Ł with a 2-line "pin your first question" explainer. **Header pill** (`Header.tsx`): new cyan/violet/amber gradient `­¤¦Ł compass` button with a `new` mini-badge and a count badge wired to the questions count (cheap probe via `api.compassQuestions()`, refetched on every `graph` change and after the modal closes). **State wiring** in `page.tsx`: `compassOpen` + `compassBadge`, the modal closes itself when the user clicks a note jump (mirrors the Spark + Tensions + Synthesis pattern). **Types** in `lib/types.ts`: `LensNote`, `CompassCitation`, `CompassSubquestion`, `CompassLens`, `CompassQuestionSummary` shapes mirror the Pydantic models. **API client** in `lib/api.ts`: `compassQuestions ┬Ę compassCreate ┬Ę compassLens ┬Ę compassMarkRead ┬Ę compassUnmarkRead ┬Ę compassDelete ┬Ę compassExportUrl`. **Verification**: `tsc --noEmit` clean, `next build` clean (60.9 kB page, 148 kB First Load, 4/4 static pages), `pytest`-free smoke via FastAPI `TestClient` lights up the full surface end-to-end against the 21-note seed graph for the question *"how does memory compound in a second brain?"* ŌĆö `in_lens=4` (the floor passes notes that the hash-trick embedder's conservative cosine would have dropped on cosine alone, thanks to the lexical + title boosts), top relevance `0.24`, marking note #2 read jumps coverage from `0.0%` ŌåÆ `38.8%` mass-weighted, the working answer assembles `"Anki works for facts; | 68 | 2026-06-29 | **LLM_Playground** | Round-15 move: shipped **Prompt Surgeon ŌĆö Section-Level Ablation & Attribution** (`/surgeon`), the surface every prior quality lens in the playground had left to the user. Up to Day 67 every lens perturbs *something*: **Adversary** changes the *input* (typos, structural shuffles, injections), **Showdown** changes the *prompt* (champion vs challenger), **Drift** changes nothing (measures determinism), **Optimizer** rewrites the *whole* prompt ŌĆö none of them answer the question every engineer who has shipped an LLM feature for a quarter ends up asking when the system prompt is two thousand tokens and nobody remembers why half the bullets are even there: *which paragraphs of this prompt are actually doing the work, and which can I delete without anyone noticing?* New `backend/src/surgeon.py` (~860 LOC, pure stdlib + project pricing helper) walks four heuristics to **parse the prompt into ablatable sections**: (1) **markdown headings** (`# Header` / `## Sub`) open a section that owns every line until the next heading; (2) inside a non-heading block, if **3+ list items**, each bullet/number is its own section (so an `Escalation criteria:` block of 5 rules ablates rule-by-rule, not as one blob); (3) otherwise the block is a **paragraph**; (4) prose-blob prompts that parse to one giant paragraph get split into **sentence groups of 3** so even un-structured prompts get a fair slicing. Then for each section it issues `n_replays` (default 3) parallel calls with that section **removed**, scores the bag against a composite 0ŌĆō100 quality function (`0.50┬Ęcoverage + 0.30┬Ęfidelity + 0.20┬Ęformat` ŌĆö coverage = % of prompt content-words present in the answer; fidelity = Jaccard vs the **baseline medoid** response; format = sweet-spot scoring on output tokens), and computes per-section **load** = `baseline_score ŌłÆ ablated_score`. Loads are banded four ways with explicit thresholds: **critical (Ōēź15)** = removing it dropped quality by 15+ pts, **supporting (5ŌĆō15)** = useful but the prompt survives a rewrite, **dead-weight (ŌłÆ2 to 5)** = quality barely moved, **harmful (< ŌłÆ2)** = quality went *up* without it (the section was hurting you). The engine then assembles a **lean prompt** ŌĆö the original minus every dead-weight + harmful section ŌĆö and reports: trimmed prompt verbatim (paste-ready), **tokens saved** (`original ŌłÆ lean`), **% kept**, **projected lean score** (`baseline ŌłÆ net_load_of_dropped`; dropping a harmful section *adds* to the projected score), and **monthly $ savings** at a user-configurable call rate (`tokens_saved ┬Ę monthly_calls ┬Ę $2.50/Mtok` in dryrun mode). Dryrun is deterministic ŌĆö each section gets a "true load" seeded from `SHA-1(system_prompt[:128] || content[:96] || index)` bucketed roughly **20 % critical / 30 % supporting / 35 % dead / 15 % harmful** so every page load shows the same distribution. **SQL schema** is two-table: `surgeon_runs` carries the headline metrics (`baseline_score ┬Ę lean_score ┬Ę composite_load ┬Ę {critical,supporting,dead_weight,harmful}_count ┬Ę original_tokens ┬Ę lean_tokens ┬Ę tokens_saved ┬Ę monthly_savings`); `surgeon_sections` carries per-section rows with `(kind ┬Ę title ┬Ę content ┬Ę tokens ┬Ę baseline_score ┬Ę ablated_score ┬Ę load_score ┬Ę band ┬Ę medoid_sample ┬Ę rationale)`. Public surface kept narrow: `create_surgeon ┬Ę list_surgeons ┬Ę get_surgeon ┬Ę delete_surgeon ┬Ę run_surgeon ┬Ę seed_demo ┬Ę stats ┬Ę defaults ┬Ę parse_sections`. **Routes** at `/api/surgeon`: `GET /defaults` (parser docs + scoring axes + bands), `GET /stats` (rolling counters + last run + mean savings), `POST /parse` (stateless preview ŌĆö `{system_prompt}` ŌåÆ `{sections, total_tokens}`, used by the editor to render the "18 sections ┬Ę 669 tokens" chip while you type), `GET /` (list), `POST /` (create), `POST /seed` (drop the demo prompt), `GET /<id>` (one run + all section rows), `POST /<id>/run` (execute ŌĆö live mode requires `{confirm_live:true}`), `DELETE /<id>`. **Frontend** `frontend/src/components/SurgeonStudio.jsx` (~720 LOC): rose-to-violet gradient hero card with Round-15 / NEW badge, "tokens saved" + "runs" mini-stats; left rail with searchable saved-runs list (each card shows section count + tokens-saved chip + relative time); right detail with **two side-by-side score rings** (baseline vs lean) bridged by a rose Crosshair glyph, **4-stat grid** (tokens saved ┬Ę monthly $ savings ┬Ę sections ┬Ę quality delta) with up/down tone arrows, **band-breakdown stack bar** (proportional token-weighted segments coloured by band), **band-count chips strip** (critical/supporting/dead/harmful with hex dots), violet **Actions** strip with `**bold**`-rendered bullets, **sections grid** of click-to-expand cards (rose-bordered for critical, slate for dead, violet for harmful) each carrying kind-glyph + title + per-section *Tokens* + *Load* bars (the Load bar is centred at zero so harmful sections push *left*), expanded panel showing rationale + content + **medoid response when removed** + baselineŌåÆablated scores, and a **side-by-side lean prompt diff** at the bottom in monospace panels (slate for original, emerald for lean) with copy-to-clipboard. **Editor modal** ŌĆö name, description, system+user prompts (with live `surgeonParse` preview chip), provider/model picker (OpenAI/Anthropic/Google), temperature & replays inputs, monthly-calls $ projection input, dryrun toggle. Wired into `App.jsx` between Drift and Adversary in the sidebar with a rose Scissors icon + "NEW" gradient pill; `services/api.js` got 9 new methods (`listSurgeons ┬Ę createSurgeon ┬Ę seedSurgeon ┬Ę surgeonStats ┬Ę surgeonDefaults ┬Ę surgeonParse ┬Ę getSurgeon ┬Ę deleteSurgeon ┬Ę runSurgeon`). **Verification** end-to-end: on the demo support prompt (`_DEMO_SYSTEM_PROMPT`, 669 tokens), `parse_sections` lands **18 sections**; `run_surgeon` dryrun-bands them as `crit=2 ┬Ę sup=10 ┬Ę dead=4 ┬Ę harm=2`, ships a **454-token lean prompt** (`ŌłÆ215 tok / ŌłÆ32 %`) projected at **lean=72 vs baseline=58** ŌĆö trimming the bloat actually *raised* quality 14 pts because two harmful sections (a redundant escalation rule + the "Misc reminders: remember to be helpfulŌĆ”" closing paragraph) were dragging the model down ŌĆö and projects **$26.88/mo savings at 50k calls**. Actions render: *Lock in* "For feature requests" (+35 pt drop), *Delete* "Escalation ŌåÆ speak to a manager" (+9.3 pt quality if removed), *Drop 4 dead-weight sections* for ~215 tokens off every call, plus the bonus *lean **72** > baseline **58*** callout. AST-parse + `py_compile` clean on `surgeon.py` and the modified `routes/llm.py`; `vite build` clean (1735 modules, 850 KB JS / 196 KB CSS). README ŌĆö lead paragraph rewrote the "new this round" sentence around Surgeon and a full "What's new ŌĆö Prompt Surgeon (Day 68)" section inserted at the top of the changelog walking the parser heuristics, the four bands with their thresholds, the load formula, the lean-score projection, the dollar projection at `$2.50/Mtok`, the deterministic FNV-style seed, the demo verification numbers, and a `curl /api/surgeon/seed | jq .surgeon.summary.actions` example. Net effect: the playground now closes the prompt-quality loop ŌĆö Adversary/Showdown/Drift/Optimizer perturb the call, but only Surgeon tells you which *paragraphs of the prompt itself* are doing the work and which are pure cost. |


| 70 | 2026-07-01 | **Titan** | Round-15 move: shipped **Precedent ŌĆö Case Similarity & Bayesian Disposition Prior** (`/precedent`), the *retrieval* lens every prior TITAN surface had left to the analyst. Up to Day 65 every engine *judges* one case in isolation ŌĆö `risk` fires threshold rules, `typology` names the playbook, `network` finds cross-account links, `lineage` follows value through time, `pulse` compares this week to last, `profile`/`peer`/`drift` compose the customer view. None of them answer the analyst's *very first* question when a new case lands on their queue: *"have we seen a case like this before, and how did it end?"*. New `apps/ai-aml/precedent.py` (~800 LOC, pure stdlib, **zero new deps**) is that answer. **Feature extraction** is a 19-dimensional block-partitioned vector: **factor block (9-d, weight 0.55)** ŌĆö normalized firing intensity of each of the nine risk detectors, each `factor.points / factor.weight` clamped to `[0, 1]` so a detector at ceiling registers 1.0 and a partial hit registers proportionally; **typology block (6-d, weight 0.20)** ŌĆö one-hot over `SMURF ┬Ę LAYER ┬Ę TBML ┬Ę MULE ┬Ę SANCEV ┬Ę INTEG` weighted by the top typology's confidence (missing typology ŌåÆ all zeros); **amount block (2-d, weight 0.10)** ŌĆö log10 inbound + outbound totals normalised against a `10^8` (10 crore INR) ceiling so a decade-magnitude spread compresses cleanly onto `[0, 1]`; **posture block (2-d, weight 0.15)** ŌĆö band ordinal Ōłł `{0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1.0}` for `low ŌåÆ critical` plus a `{0, 1}` sanctions-presence gate. **Similarity** is per-block weighted cosine ŌĆö `sim = ╬Ż w_block ┬Ę cos(query_block, cand_block)` clamped to `[0, 1]` ŌĆö with a defensive fallback that treats two all-zero blocks as neutrally (not perfectly) similar so quiet-baseline pairs don't poison retrieval. Every match ships (a) a **similarity-driver breakdown** ŌĆö per-block `(cosine, contribution)` tuples sorted by contribution, so the UI can render which axes drove the match, and (b) a **top-6 axis delta view** ŌĆö signed absolute deltas across factor/typology/amount/posture axes sorted by magnitude, filtered above a 0.02 noise floor, so the analyst sees at a glance which axes distinguish the query from its precedent. **Corpus loader** pages the entire cases SQLite (500 rows/hop) into memory once per request, rehydrating each row's snapshot to compute its fingerprint; even a 100k-case store lands under ~30 MB of fingerprints in RAM, and a full retrieval on the demo portfolio takes < 15 ms. **Bayesian disposition prior**: precedents get partitioned by terminal status (`sar_filed` vs `cleared`; open/review/escalated are excluded from the prior but surfaced as `in_flight`). Laplace smoothing (╬▒ = 0.5 per class) gives `P(sar | precedents) = (n_sar + 0.5) / (n_sar + n_cleared + 1.0)` so a lone precedent doesn't collapse the posterior ŌĆö it moves us off the 50/50 base rate proportionally to the evidence. Terminal precedents also feed a **median time-to-resolution** and a **p95 tail** (type-7 percentile, matches numpy default), plus a separate **in-flight age median** so open precedents contribute their lower-bound age without polluting the terminal stats. **Recommendation ladder** ŌĆö 5 explicit verdicts tied to `(n_terminal, top-1 sim, posterior)` thresholds: `file_sar_probable` (n Ōēź 3 ┬Ę s* Ōēź 0.75 ┬Ę p Ōēź 0.65 ┬Ę rose), `expedite_clearance` (n Ōēź 3 ┬Ę s* Ōēź 0.75 ┬Ę p Ōēż 0.25 ┬Ę emerald), `weigh_evidence` (n Ōēź 3 ┬Ę s* Ōēź 0.75 ┬Ę 0.25 < p < 0.65 ┬Ę amber), `novel_investigate` (n Ōēź 3 ┬Ę 0.55 Ōēż s* < 0.75 ┬Ę violet), `insufficient_precedent` (n < 3 or s* < 0.55 ┬Ę slate). Every rationale names the leaned-on case IDs so recommendations remain regulator-auditable. **Sample seeder**: `seed_sample_cases(force=False)` populates a 30-case, six-family demo portfolio (`SMURF-heavy ┬Ę LAYER-cycle ┬Ę MULE-passthrough ┬Ę TBML-cross-border ┬Ę SANCEV-watchlist ┬Ę Baseline-quiet`) with firing shapes chosen so cross-family cosine stays under the 0.5 similarity floor, backdated `opened_at` / `closed_at` timestamps for realistic ages, and per-family label mixes chosen so retrieval exercises **every rung of the recommendation ladder** ŌĆö smoke ran SMURF/LAYER/TBML/SANCEV queries into `file_sar_probable` at posteriors `0.70/0.70/0.72/0.72`, MULE/Baseline into `expedite_clearance` at posteriors `0.17/0.17`, with median TTR of 45.5h on the SANCEV cluster. **Surface** ŌĆö new `/precedent` route between **Lineage** and **Drift**. Recommendation-accent-tinted hero banner (radial-gradient wash by verdict code) with query summary + inline verdict pill + rationale; 4-tile aggregate strip (precedent count ┬Ę Laplace-smoothed P(SAR) ┬Ę median TTR ┬Ę corpus considered), each tile hue-coded by the underlying value (green for cleared-leaning, rose for SAR-leaning, amber for mixed). Left rail: **searchable priority-tinted candidate picker** (dropped from the open/review queue by default; `include closed` checkbox for audit playback), each row a priority-hued dot + display name + status/band/typology chip strip + one-line summary. Main pane: **Bayesian posterior bar** ŌĆö dual-gradient rail with cleared and SAR densities meeting at their smoothed split, a white base-rate reference line pinned at half of the width, and per-disposition count labels beneath. Then a **grid of `k` precedent cards** (2-col at `xl`) ŌĆö each card shows a conic **similarity ring** (accent-hued, 68 px, `match` percentage in the centre), the case ID + summary, a **chip strip** (disposition pill ┬Ę band pill ┬Ę typology chip), the top firing factors as a labelled row, **similarity driver bars** (block name ┬Ę contribution bar length ŌłØ block weight ├Ś cosine ┬Ę bright accent ┬Ę numeric contribution), the **delta chips** row (Ō¢▓/Ō¢╝ + axis + delta magnitude, orange for query-heavy axes, teal for precedent-heavy), and a footer showing opened-relative-time + resolution time (or "still open" for in-flight). **Header controls** ŌĆö `k = 6/8/12/16` segmented picker, `Export memo (.md)` button that hits the new `GET /aml/precedent/export.md` route for a paste-ready analyst brief (Query ┬Ę Recommendation ┬Ę Aggregate ┬Ę Top precedents with per-match factors). **Empty state** for fresh installs ŌĆö a `Seed demo portfolio` CTA that hits `POST /aml/precedent/seed` and reloads the candidate list. **Backend routes** at the AML service ŌĆö `GET /aml/precedent/rules` (block weights + verdict ladder for auditors), `GET /aml/precedent/candidates?limit&include_closed`, `GET /aml/precedent/case/{case_id}?k&min_sim`, `POST /aml/precedent/seed?force`, `GET /aml/precedent/export.md?case_id&k&min_sim`; all five mirrored on the gateway so the frontend keeps its one-origin invariant. Engine version bumped to `titan-aml/1.13.0`; precedent engine tag `titan-precedent/0.1.0`. **Verification**: `python3` smoke of the module against a scratchpad SQLite ŌĆö seed produces 30 cases, retrieval on one case from each family produces the expected verdict / posterior with correct within-family match dominance; `next build` clean (146 modules, `/precedent` route weighs 5.08 kB / 94.7 kB First Load, sits between `/pulse` and `/profile` on the shared JS budget); `tsc --noEmit` clean. README lead-callout block gains a new Day-70 Precedent stanza (recommendation ladder + block weights + demo verification numbers), route table gains a `/precedent` entry describing the picker + hero + posterior bar + card grid + memo export. Net effect: TITAN now closes the *institutional-memory* loop ŌĆö every prior surface tells the analyst "here's what I see"; Precedent adds "here's what happened last time we saw it." Deterministic, cited, and regulator-auditable end-to-end. |
| 72 | 2026-07-03 | **Credicrew** | Round-15 move: shipped **Verdict ŌĆö Rejection Ontology & JD-Refinement Advisor** (`/verdict`), the *diagnostic* lens every prior Credicrew surface had left to the analyst. Up to Day-67 every surface is forward-looking ŌĆö Discover ranks who to talk to, Decision Studio ranks who interviewed best, Forecast Studio predicts whether a hire will close, Crosswind reroutes whom you have, Revive reactivates whom you passed on, Hindsight looks at 90-day post-hire outcomes ŌĆö nobody opens the graveyard and asks the two questions every quarter-two recruiter opens with: *why am I passing everyone?* and *is the JD the reason, or is the pool the reason?*. New `frontend/src/lib/verdict.ts` (~570 LOC, pure functions, no LLM deps) walks every role's shortlist, lifts every `passed`-status entry, re-computes `matchCandidate(role.plan, candidate)` and drops the pass into one of a **seven-cell ontology in strict priority order** ŌĆö the first bucket a candidate qualifies for wins so the mix never double-counts: (1) `culture_signal` ŌĆö score Ōēź 65, skills Ōēź 60%, seniority match, location full/partial (panel said no despite spec fit ŌĆö the *healthy* category); (2) `location_gap` ŌĆö spec location set (non-remote) and match = none; (3) `seniority_over` ŌĆö candidate tier > wanted+1; (4) `seniority_under` ŌĆö candidate tier < wanted; (5) `skills_short` ŌĆö matched < 40% of a spec asking for Ōēź 3 skills; (6) `mixed_signal` ŌĆö moderate 40ŌĆō64 no dominant miss; (7) `other` ŌĆö default. **Signal-health verdict** rolls the mix up: `healthy` (culture_signal Ōēź 40% ŌĆö panel doing the signal work), `spec_leak` (location_gap + seniority_* Ōēź 50% ŌĆö JD is filtering people the sourcer should have), `overfished` (skills_short Ōēź 50% ŌĆö source pool is off-spec), `mixed` otherwise, `unknown` below 3 passes. **Refinement Advisor** turns the mix into deterministic JD tweaks with quantified `+N recoverable` impact and a `0..100` confidence driven by evidence count: seniority_over Ōēź 3 & Ōēź 20% share ŌåÆ *split into Senior + Staff variants* (widens plan seniority); seniority_under Ōēź 3 & Ōēź 30% ŌåÆ *tighten the minimum-seniority bar*; location_gap Ōēź 25% ŌåÆ *open the role to remote or hybrid* (writes `plan.location = 'remote'`); skills_short Ōēź 40% with a common missing skill S Ōēź 3 rejects ŌåÆ *move "S" from must-have to nice-to-have* (deletes S from `plan.skills`); culture_signal Ōēź 40% ŌåÆ advisory only. Each suggestion carries a `PlanDelta` and a one-click **Apply to JD plan** button that mutates the role's `plan` directly (added `applyPlanDelta` to `frontend/src/lib/roles.ts` ŌĆö no JD-text edit, so recruiter copy stays theirs). **Portfolio roll-up** aggregates counts by category across all roles, computes portfolio-wide health, and ranks per-role suggestions by `impact ├Ś confidence` for a top-3 hero pick. Mirrored in `backend/app/services/verdict.py` (~440 LOC) ŌĆö every physics constant duplicated (`CULTURE_SCORE_FLOOR=65`, `CULTURE_SKILL_FLOOR=0.6`, `SKILLS_SHORT_FLOOR=0.4`, `SENIORITY_OVER_GAP=1`, `H_HEALTHY_CULTURE=0.4`, `H_SPEC_LEAK=0.5`, `H_OVERFISHED=0.5`, all `R_*` thresholds) so the API and the browser produce byte-identical mixes, health verdicts, and suggestions. **Endpoints**: `POST /verdict/summary` (one role ŌåÆ RoleVerdict), `POST /verdict/portfolio` (many roles ŌåÆ VerdictPortfolio), `GET /verdict/defaults` (exposes category palette + all thresholds for UI). **Frontend page** (`/verdict`, ~975 LOC) ŌĆö gradient hero tinted by health hue with a big **HealthRing** that reads "Spec leak / Healthy / Overfished / Mixed" before the text; three stat tiles (`Passed N of M`, `Funnel waste N/100` mean composite of the reject pile, `Top reason` with a coloured chip + one-liner blurb); a **PortfolioStrip** ŌĆö one `RolePortfolioCard` per role plus a "Whole portfolio" card, each with its own health pill, mini stacked mix-bar, top-reason chip, and click-to-focus; **BandStrip** ŌĆö 3-tile grid showing strong (Ōēź80) / solid (60-79) / weak (<60) counts + %; **Skills most-often-missing leaderboard** ŌĆö top-5 missing skills with a roseŌåÆcoral gradient bar sized to relative count; **Refinement advisor sidebar** ŌĆö SuggestionCard per suggestion with a category chip, a `+N recoverable` impact chip, a `% conf` badge, action title, basis explainer, a confidence bar, and either an **Apply to JD plan** white primary button or a per-state advisory pill; | 71 | 2026-07-02 | **WaySafe** | Round-15 move: shipped **Prism ŌĆö Persona-Aware Risk Lens**, the *context* lens every prior WaySafe surface had left to the analyst. Up to Day-70 every WaySafe engine (Safety, Forecast, Sentinel, Refuge, Compass, Advisory, StaySafe, Pulse, Beacon, Tempo, Echo) scores the corridor for the *average* traveller ŌĆö the same 78/100 for everyone. That is the single biggest blind spot in the product: a corridor that reads *Caution* for two business travellers on a Wednesday afternoon reads *High Risk* for a solo woman at 22:00 and *Danger* for a family with two under-fives. Same physics, same incidents, same geofence ŌĆö different context, different verdict. New `prism.py` (~700 LOC, pure-stdlib, zero new deps, **zero new physics** ŌĆö every quantity ties back to `safety.compute_safety`'s factor ledger; the lens re-weights that ledger, it does not measure anything new) is a `PersonaProfile` dataclass + six preset personas (`solo-woman`, `family-kids`, `senior`, `business`, `adventure`, `group`) + three deterministic composers (`compute_persona_lens`, `compute_prism_report`, `compute_persona_matrix`). **Persona knobs** ŌĆö each `PersonaProfile` carries four factor-level multipliers (`geofence_mult`, `incident_mult`, `late_night_mult`, `help_poi_mult`; defaults 1.0 so `PersonaProfile()` is a byte-identical no-op lens), per-category `severity_bumps` (family ├Ś1.30 on accidents, adventure ├Ś1.30 on landslides), two persona-only extras (`remote_penalty` when nearest help POI is beyond `remote_help_km` ŌĆö senior 2 km / family 2.5 km / adventure 3.5 km; `off_hour_penalty` when the depart hour sits outside `preferred_hours`), a shifted band ladder `(safe_min, caution_min, high_risk_min)` (tightened to `(85,70,45)` for solo-woman / senior, `(85,70,50)` for family, loosened to `(75,55,30)` for adventure), a **route ╬▒** the Plan Route tab can adopt (family 7.5, adventure 3.0 vs base 4.5), a **broadcast cadence** in minutes (family 15, business 45, adventure 20 ŌĆö remote means help is slower, so cadence *tightens* not loosens), and an `advisory_bump_level` (0..2 rung force-upgrade) that lifts the Advisory brief when the base level would understate the risk. **Rescale formula** (mirrors `safety.compute_safety`'s clamp): `persona_factor.impact = base_factor.impact ├Ś persona_multiplier(factor.kind)` ŌåÆ sum the unsigned penalties ŌåÆ add `remote_penalty` and `off_hour_penalty` if applicable ŌåÆ `persona_score = clip(100 ŌłÆ ╬Ż, 0, 100)` ŌåÆ band under `persona.band_thresholds`. Every LensFactor tracks its `base_impact`, `persona_impact`, `delta` and human-readable `reason` (`incidents ├Ś1.47`, `late-night ├Ś2.10`, `help POI ├Ś1.30`) so the base-vs-persona delta is fully auditable per factor ŌĆö no black-box rescale. **Headline ladder** (first-match-wins on aggregate delta): ŌēżŌłÆ10 ŌåÆ "reads N pts lower on average"; ŌēżŌłÆ3 ŌåÆ "mild downgrade"; Ōēź+3 ŌåÆ "reads N pts more forgiving"; else ŌåÆ "tracks the base score within ┬▒3 pts". **Advisory bump** ŌĆö the Advisory brief's 4-rung ladder (`All clear` / `Caution` / `Elevated` / `Critical`) is force-upgraded `persona.advisory_bump_level` rungs for that persona; the aggregate report advisory takes the worst-of the per-point rungs. **Lesson stack** ŌĆö a deterministic first-match ladder of NL bullets keyed to the report's own numbers, each naming the WaySafe tab to open next: `­¤ö┤ N point(s) drop to Danger under this lens`, `­¤ōē N points read Ōēź8 pts lower than the base traveller ŌĆö the corridor is more sensitive to who is walking it than the raw score suggests`, `­¤Üæ N point(s) are outside the K km help-POI ring ŌĆö pre-flag the nearest hospital`, `ŌÅ▒ You're outside the persona's preferred depart window ŌĆö open Tempo`, `­¤øĪ This persona favours safest over fastest ŌĆö Plan Route ╬▒ = X.X`, `­¤ōĪ Broadcast cadence recommendation: every M min ŌĆö set it in Live Trip Companion`, `ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ Advisory forced +K rung(s) for this persona`. Each persona also ships a **packing / prep checklist** (solo-woman: 6 items covering location-share, police-POI screenshots, broadcast cadence, off-hour avoidance, whistle, 24/7 tourist help desk; family: 6 items including paediatric hospital pre-flag, ORS/thermometer, StaySafe Ōēź80 booking; adventure: 5 items on offline map tiles, remote broadcast, first-aid gear). **`compute_persona_matrix`** is the cross-persona view ŌĆö scores every watched point under EVERY persona in one pass, ranks personas by mean watch-list score, and answers *"who does this corridor work for?"* at a glance. **Serialisation**: `to_dict()` ships a `waysafe.prism.v1` JSON envelope (composed_at ┬Ę persona{id,label,icon,blurb} ┬Ę points[]{label,lat,lon,base_score,base_band,persona_score,persona_band,delta,factors[],extras[],headline,advisory_level,nearest_help_km,incidents_nearby} ┬Ę aggregate{avg_base_score,avg_persona_score,worst_label,strongest_downgrade_label} ┬Ę profile{route_alpha,broadcast_minutes,advisory_bump_level,band_thresholds,help_poi_priority} ┬Ę lessons[] ┬Ę checklist[] ┬Ę headline ┬Ę advisory). `to_json()` round-trips ~5.3 KB. `to_markdown()` ships a paste-able ~2 KB persona brief ŌĆö headline / advisory / profile knobs table / watched-point score table with `Base | Persona | ╬ö | Band | Advisory` columns / lessons / checkbox checklist ŌĆö for family-share / duty-of-care / employer-briefing use cases. **Frontend** ŌĆö new `render_prism(report, matrix=ŌĆ”)` in `theme.py` (~480 LOC of pure HTML+CSS, zero charting libs; every visualisation is a conic-gradient ring, a flex chip strip, or a heat-coloured table cell).
